┼ЪR─АDDHA

This subject is of great practical importance from several points of view.

The Brahmapur├вna defines ┼Ыr─Бddha as follows: ‘whatever is given with faith to br─Бhmaс╣Зas intending it to be for the (benefit of) pitrs at a proper time, in a proper place, to deserv ing persons and in accordance with the prescribed procedure is called sraddha.751. The Mit. on Yaj. I. 217 definessraddha as ‘abandonment with faith of an article of food or some sub stitute thereof, intending it for (the benefit of) the departed’. The Kalpataru on sr─Бddha defined it as ’the giving up of sacri. ficial material intending it for pitys and its acceptance by br─Бhmanas’. The Sr─Бddhaviveka of Rudradhara and the ┼Ъr─Бd dhaprak─Б┼Ыa define ┼Ыr─Бddha in the same way as the Mit, but in a more involved manner. Yaj. I. 268 (= Agnipurana 163. 40-41) states that the pitrs viz. Vasus, Rudras and Adityas that are the deities of ┼Ыr─Бddha, being gratified by ┼Ыr─Бddha, give gratification to the ancestors of human beings. This verse and Manu III. 284 make it clear that the three ancestors of a man,

Definition of ┼Ыr─Бddha

viz, the father, paternal grand-father and the paternal great grand-father are respectively to be identified with the three orders of superintending pit; deities, viz. Vasus, Rudras and Adityas, when performing ┼Ыr─Бddha. According to some,752 ┼Ыr├дddha denotes three things, viz. homa, the offering of pinda (ball of cooked food) and gratification of br─Бhmaс╣Зas invited to a dinner; the application of this word to any one of these three can only be in a secondary sense.

A firm believer in the doctrine of karma, punarjanma (re incarnation) and karma-vip─Бka (explained above) may find it difficult to reconcile that doctrine with the belief that by offer ing balls of rice to his three deceased paternal ancestors a man brings gratification to the souls of the latter. According to the doctrine of punarjanma (as very clearly and succinctly put in Br. Up. IV. 4.4 and Bhagavad-git─Б 2.22) 753 the spirit leaving one body enters into another and a new one. But the doctrine of offering balls of rice to three ancestors requires that the spirits of the three ancestors even after the lapse of 50 or 100 years are still capable of enjoying in an ethereal body the flavour or essence of the rice balls wafted by the wind. Further, Y─Бj. I. 269 (which is the same as M─Бrk. 29. 38, Matsya-pur─Б┼Жa 19. 11-12, Agnipur─Бna 163. 41-42) provides that the grand fathers (i. e. pitrs) being themselves gratified (by the offerings of food in sr─Бddha) bestow on men (their descendants ) long life, progeny, wealth, learning, heaven, mok┼Яa (final beatitude), all happiness and kingdom. In the Matsya-pur─Б┼Жa (chap. 19, verse 2) a question is asked by the sages how food which a br─Бhmana (invited at a ┼Ыr─Бddha) eats or which is offered into fire is enjoyed by departed spirits that might have assumed (after death) good or evil forms of bodies. The answer given ( verses 3-9) is that fathers, grand-fathers and great-grand fathers are identified with Vasus, Rudras and Adityas respectively according to Vedic passages, that the name and gotra (mentioned at the time of ┼Ыr├дddha), the mantras uttered and faith carry to the pitys the offerings made, that if one’s

IV)

Does ┼Ыr─Бddha serve no purpose

337

to perform it or is it because sraddha produces no consequences or is it that it is not proved that pitrs and the rest are gratified by ┼Ыr─Бddha? To the first he replies that there are such passages as ’therefore a wise man must perform ┼Яr─Бddha with all his efforts that lay down the obligation; nor is the 2nd objection proper, since Y─Бj. I. 269 does declare the rewards (of ┼Ыr─Бddha ) viz, long life &c. Nor is the third alternative acceptable. In the ┼Ыr─Бddha rites it is not that the mere ancestors named Deva datta and the like are the recipients and that they are denoted by the words pitr, pit├дmaha and prapit─Бmaha, but that those words denote them as accompanied by the superintending deities viz. Vasus, Rudras and Adityas. Just as by the words Deva datta and the like what is denoted is not merely the bodies ( so named) nor merely the souls, but what is denoted by the words is individual souls as particularised by the bodies; in the same way the words pit? and the like denote Devadatta and others together with the superintending deities (viz. Vasus, Rudras and Adityas). Therefore, the superintending deities viz, the Vasus and the rest, being gratified by the food and drink offered by the sons and the rest, gratify those also viz. Davadatta and the rest and endow the performers (of ┼Ыr─Бddha ) with such rewards as male progeny and the rest. Just as a. woman expecting to be a mother becomes gratified by partaking of the food and drink for which she has a longing in pregnancy and which is given to her by another person for the sustenance of the child in the womb, she satiates also the child in her womb and endows those that offer her the food and drink for which she has longings by bestowing on them some reward in return. Thus the pitss denoted by the words father, grand father and great-grand-father are the deities Vasus, Rudras and Adityas, and not merely (human beings called ) Devadatta and the rest. Hence these deities of ┼Ыr─Бddha become the recipients (of gifts) in the ┼Ыr─Бddha rite, are gratified by the ┼Ыr─Бddha and gratify in their turn the ancestors of human beings. The Sr─Бddha-kalpalat─Б then quotes 18 verses 756 from the

History of Dharma┼Ы─Бstra

[Vol.

M─Бrkandeyapur─Бpa many of which are found in chap. 28 ( verses 3 ff) of the printed text. It is said 757 that just as a calf finds its own mother from among many cows that are scattered about, so the mantras repeated in sr─Бddha carry the food to the pit┼Щs.

The explanation offered by the ┼Ъr─Бddha-kalpalat─Б relying on passages of the M─Бrkandeyapur─Бna is not satisfactory and is rather far-fetched. The M─Бrkandeya and the Matsya appear to agree with the doctrine of Ved─Бnta that immediately on leaving one body the soul has recourse to another body, either as a god or a man or a beast or a snake &c. The hypothesis pro pounded is that the food and drink offered in ┼бr─Бddhas becomes transformed into various substances for the use of the ancestors (Matsya 141. 74тАУ75). But the great difficulty in accepting this explanation is that the ancestors might die at different places, while ┼Ыr─Бddha may very often be performed at one place far away from those places. It is difficult to believe that the grass growing in one place where the ancestor has been transformed into a beast as a result of his evil actions is the same that might have been produced from the substances offered in ┼Ыr├дddha at a place hundreds of miles away. Further, if one or all the three ancestors have been transformed into beasts or the like how can they recognize their offspring and bestow on them long life, wealth &c? If the Vasus, Rudras and Adityas bestow these, it is better to say so directly and affirm that pitrs cannot bestow

It appears very probable that the worship of ancestors by means of ┼Ыr─Бddhas was a very ancient institution and that the doctrines of punarjanma and karmavip─Бka were comparatively later ones and that Hinduism being all-embracing retained the institution of ┼Ыr─Бddhas while adopting also the doctrine of metempsychosis. The institution of sr─Бddha is from one point of view an excellent one. It provides an occasion for remembrance of one’s ancestors and relatives that were dear and near when living. The Aryasam─Бja objects to the institution of sraddha and interprets pitrs in the Rgveda as meaning living men in the V─Бnapragtha stage. It may be noted that the texts support both views. The ┼аat. Br. expressly says that food is offered to the father of the sacrificer in the words ’this is for thee.’ Vi┼Яnu Dh. S. 75. 4 “He whose father is dead may put down a pinda for his father &c. On the other hand Manu III, 284 states that fathers are spoken of as Vasus, grandfathers as Rudras &c. and Y─Бj. I. 269 provides that Vasus, Rudras and Adityas are the pitrs and the devat─Бs of ┼Ыr─Бddha. These latter are to be explained as con taining an injunction to contemplate upon the pitrs as Vasus, Rudras &c.

As stated below (p. 347) with regard to the Rgvedic passages, it was on account of the supposed power of pitrs to benefit or harm the living that the cult of the dead became a prominent feature in primitive societies. Offerings and ceremonies which may have in most ancient times been prompted in part at least by the desire to placate the ancestors are continued as tokens of pure affection and remembrance. Various beliefs about pitrs are mentioned 758 in post-Vedic Literature. The Baud. Dh, S. II. 8. 14 summarizes a br─Бhmana text stating that pitrs move about in the form of birds. The Au┼бanasa-smrti and Devala quoted by the Kalpataru say the same thing. In the V─Бyu pur─Бna 759 it is stated that at the time of ┼Ыr├дddha the ancestors

enter the br─Бhmanas (invited) after assuming an aerial form and that when the best of br─Бhmaс╣Зas are honoured with clothes, foods, gifts, eatables, liquids, cows, horses and villages, pitrs become pleased. Manu III. 189 and the Au┼бanasa-smrti also support this notion that pitrs enter the invited br─Бhmaс╣Зas. The Matsyapurana (18. 5-7 ) enjoins: pindas should be offered to the departed for twelve days after death, since they serve hin as food on his journey and give him great satisfaction. Therefore, the soul leaving the dead body is not taken to the abode of the departed for twelve days after death); the departed spirit hovers near his house, his sons, his wife for twelve days. Therefore for ten days after death milk (and water) should be placed (hung up) in space for ten nights for reducing all torments (or troubles of the departed) and for the removal of the fatigue of the journey (that the departed spirit has to make ). The Vi┼Яnudharmas┼лtra 760 (20.34-36 ) provides тАЬthe departed spirit enjoys in the world of pitrs the food offered in sr─Бddha with the utterance of the word ‘svadh─Б’; whether the departed is in the state of a god or in the place of torments (Hell) or in the form of a lower animal or a human being, the ┼Ыr├дddha food offered by his relatives reaches him; when ┼Ыr─Бddha is performed, the performer and the departed soul both certainly secure vigour (or prosperity ).тАЭ

The Brahmapur─Б┼Жa 761 states that ┼Ыr─Бddha is to be treated of under five heads, viz. how, where, when, by whom and with what materials. But before proceeding to deal with these five heads, it is necessary to dilate upon the underlying ideas and significance of the word ‘pitarah’ from the most ancient times of which we have literary records.

The word ‘pitr’ means ‘father’, but the word ‘pitarah’ is used in two senses, viz. (1) a man’s three immediate deceased ancestors, (2) the early or ancient ancestors of the human race that were supposed to inhabit a separate world (loka) by them

IV)

The World of Pitrs

it is said that the pitrs dwell in the third world from this. This means that after bh┼лloka and antariksa comes the pitsloka. In the Br. Up. I. 5.16 three worlds of men, pitrs and gods are separately mentioned. In Rg. X. 135. 1-7, Yama is spoken of in somewhat different language. He is in this hymn men tioned as a god by himself and not as the first mortal who made a path (Rg. X. 14. 2) or as the gatherer of men (X. 14.1) or as being in company of the pitrs. In a few other places Yama is no doubt called r─Бjan and praised in the same breath with Varupa (Rg. X. 14,7). But such a position is very rarely mentioned, For the further development of Yama and his assistants as the punishers of men for evil deeds, vide pp. 159-160 above and notes 381-386.

There is another division of pitrs viz. pitaraс╕е somavantaс╕е,771 pitaraс╕е barhi ┼Яadah, pitarah agni┼Яv─Бtt─Бс╕е. The latter two are named in Rg. X. 15. 4 and 11 (which occur also in Tai. S. II, 6. 12. 2). The Sat. Br. defines these as follows:-“those that performed a soma sacrifice are pitaraс╕е somavantah; those that offered cooked oblations (like caru and purod─Бsa) and secured a world are pitarah barhi sadah; those that did none of these (two actions) and whom fire consumes when burning them are ’ pitarah agni┼Яv─Бtt─Бс╕е;’ these are the only ones that are pitarah.” The Tai.772 Br. has a somewhat similar passage and the K─Бthaka Samhita IX. 6. 17 also refers to these three kinds of pitrs. Later writers introduced certain changes in the mean ings of the words for the different classes of pitys and also in creased the number of the classes of pitys. (III, 193-198) mentions several classes of pitys, connects pitrs called Somap─Бs, Havirbhujaс╕е ─Аjyap─Бs and Suk─Бlins with the four varnas and in III, 199 states that the pitrs of br─Бh manas are designated as Anagnidagdha, Agnidagdha, K─Бvya, Barhi┼Яad, Agni┼Яv─Бtta and Saumya. Those verses of Manu appear to summarize different traditions about the several classes of pitys. Vide Matsyapur─Б┼Жa 141. 4 for the same last four names and 141. 15-18 for their definitions. In S─Гt─Бtapa smrti (VI. 5тАУ6) twelve groups or divisions of pilys are mentioned viz. pindabh─Бjaс╕е (three), lepabh─Бjaс╕е (three), N─Бndimukhas (three) and A┼Ыrumukhas (three). This is a classification of pitrs from two different standpoints. In V├бyu 72,1 and 73.60, Brahm─Бnda (Upodgh─Бta 9.53), Padma V. 9. 2-3, Vi┼Яnudharmo ttara I. 138. 2-3 and other Pur─Бс╣Зas the classes of pitrs are said to be seven, three of which are formless (am┼лrti mat) and four have forms (m┼лrtimat) and they and their offspring are des cribed in detail. All this is passed over here. The Skanda pur─Б┼Жa (VI. 216. 9-10) speaks of nine groups of pitrs, being Agni ┼Яv─Бtt─Бс╕е, Barhi┼Яadaс╕е, ─Аjyap─Бс╕е, Somap─Бс╕е, Ra┼Яmip─Бс╕е, Upah┼лt─Бс╕е, those called ‘─Бyantunah’, ‘Sr─Бddhabhujaс╕е, N─Бndimukh─Бh. In this list old and new elements are mixed up. The Indian mind often revels in divisions, sub-divisions and classifications with out much basis therefor and this is probably an illustration of that tendency. Manu (III. 201) states that from the sages the pitrs sprang, from the pitrs sprang gods and human beings and from the gods arose the whole world whether moving or immo vable. It is remarkable that here the gods are spoken of as springing from the pitrs. This is really a mere eulogy of pitrs (i. e. it is an arthav─Бda).

The pit rs were in a class apart from the gods. On the meaning of the word ‘pa├▒cajan─Бс╕е’ occurring in Rg. X. 774 53. 4.

Sankar─Бc─Бrya in his bh─Бsya on Vedantas┼лtra I. 4.12 states that the word T4 in Rg. VIII. 63.21917 means praj─Б (people).

Meaning of Pa├▒caianaс╕е

(pa├▒cajan─Б mama hotram ju┼Яadhyam) and other passages, the Ait. Br. (13.7 or 3.31) explains that they are the five classes, viz. Gandharvas with Apsarases, pitrs, devas, sarpas and r─Бk┼Яasas. The Nirukta III. 8 partly follows this explanation and also gives another. In the Atharvaveda X, 6.32 the gods, pitrs and men are mentioned in that order. The ancient Vedic texts and practice make a sharp distinction between the Gods and the Pitrs. The Tai. S. VI. 1.1.1 states: ’the gods and men divided the quarters, the gods took the east, pitrs the south, men the west and Rudras the north.’ The general rule is that sacrifices for gods are begun in the forenoon, while the pitr-yaj├▒a is performed in the afternoon (San. Br.).775 The Sat. Br. II, 4.2.2 narrates that the pitrs wearing the sacred thread over the right shoulder (and under the left arm) and bending their left knee approached Praj─Бpati, when Praj─Бpati said to them ‘you will have food at the end of) each month (on the Am─Бv─Бsy─Б), your svadh─Б (cordial) will be swiftness of thought and the moon will be your light,’ while to the gods he had said that sacrifice will be their food and the sun their light. The Tai. Br. 776 I. 3. 10.4 appears to make a distinction between pitrs who are of the nature and position of gods and pitrs that are more or less like human beings.

The Kausika-s┼лtra (1. 9-23) neatly collects in one place the difference in the procedure of the rites meant for gods and for pitrs. The performer of rites for gods wears the sacred thread on the left shoulder and under the right armpit, while in the case of the rites for pitrs it is worn on the right shoulder and under the left arm; the rite for gods is either begun facing the east or north, while that for the pitss is begun facing the south; the rite for gods is finished in the north-east (or north or east), while that for the pitys is completed in the south-west; an action is done only once for pitrs, while for gods at least thrice or as many times as the texts direct; in going round (perambulating) the right side is turned towards gods and the left one in the case of pitrs; offerings are made to gods with the words ‘sv─Бha’ and ‘va┼Яat’, while they are made to pit┼Щs with ‘svadh─Б’ and

then states that the performer mutters the words “here, O fathers! regale yourselves, like bulls come here each to his own share’ (V─Бj. S. II. 31 first half). Some (such as Tai. S. Relying on these Vedic passages and on the fact that Manu (III. 221 ) and Visnudharma s┼лtra (21. 3,75. 4) prescribe the invocation of pitrs after men tioning their gotra and names that the Sr─Бddhaprak─Б┼Ыa (p. 13) concludes that it is really the father and the other ancestors that are the deities of ┼Ыr─Бddha and not Vasu, Rudra and Aditya, since these latter have no gotra and that the description of the father and others as Vasu, Rudra and Aditya is meant only for contemplation (on them as identical with Vasus &c.). On a passage of the Brahmapur─Б┼Жa 782 prescribing that the perfor mer should say to the invited br─Бhmanas that he would call the pitrs to the rites and that when the br─Бhmaс╣Зas give per mission to call them he should do so, the ┼Ъr. The V─Бyupur─Бpa (56. 65-66) Brahm─Бnda and Anu. distinguish between pitrs who are above and pitrs who are laukika, viz. father, grand-father and great-grand-father. Vide also V─Бyu 70. 34 for pitrs that are like gods.

In the post-Vedic Literature, particularly in the Pur─Бnas, a great deal is said about the origin and classes of pitrs. For example, the V─Бyupur─Бna 56. 18 speaks of three classes of pitrs viz. ‘k├дvy├дh, barhisadah and agnisv─Бtt─Бс╕е’, while the same Pur─Бna, chap. 73, Var─Бha 13. 16 ff, Padma (Srsti 9. 2-4) and Brahm├дnda III. 10.1 speak of the origin of pitrs of seven classes that dwell in heaven, four of which have a form ( m├╝rlimat ) and three of which are without form (am┼лrta). The S─Бt─Бtapa-smrti (6. 5-6 ) speaks of 12 pitrs viz. pindabh─Бjah, lepabh─Бjah, n─Бndimukh─Бс╕е and a┼Ыrumukh─Бс╕е. All such descrip tions have to be passed over from considerations of space.

Bhandarkar Oriental Research InstituteIV)

Promulgators of ┼Ыr─Бddha rites

349

From the s┼лtra period ( about 600 B.C.) to the most modern among medieval Dharma┼Ы─Бstra works the authors wax eloquent over the praises or the importance or benefits of the institution of ┼Ыr─Бddhas. One of the earliest works among these, viz. the Ap. Dh. S. gives the following interesting information : 783 тАЬFormerly men and gods lived together in this world. The gods went to heaven owing to sacrifices (i. e, as a reward of sacrifices that they performed), but men remained behind. Those among men who perform sacrifices in the same way as the gods did, dwell in the other world (i. e. heaven) with the gods and Brahman. Then (seeing that men lagged behind) Manu promulgated the rite which is designated by the word ‘┼Ыr─Бddha’ and which tends to the salvation (or happiness) of mankind. In this rite the Manes (pitaraс╕е) are the deities but the br─Бhmaс╣Зas (that are fed) are in the place of the ─Бhavaniya fire (in which in sacrifices to gods oblations are offered)”. On account of this last s┼лtra Haradatta (com, of ─Аp. Dh, S.) and others hold that feeding the br─Бhmaс╣Зas is the princi pal act at a ┼Ыr─Бddha. The Brahm─Бndapur─Б┼Жa (Upodgh─Бtap─Бda 9. 15. and 10. 99) speaks of Manu as the promulgator of ┼Ыr─Бddha rites and Vis┼Жupur─Б┼Жa III. 1. 30, V─Бyu 44. 38 and Bh─Бgavata III. 1, 22 designate Manu as Sr─Бddha-deva, Similarly, in the S├дntiparva 345.784 14-21 and the Visnu-dharmottara I.139.14-16 it is stated that the institution of ┼Ыr─Бddha was established in the Boar incarnation by Visnu and that Vispu should be regarded as dwelling in the three pindas offered to the father, grand-father and great-grandfather. From this and from the passage of the Ap. Dh. S. cited above we may infer that it was believed even several centuries before Christ that the institution of ┼Ыr─Бddhas had a hoary antiquity behind it and that it was as old as Manu, the father of mankind according to the Rgveda (VIII. 63.1, VIII. 30. 3.). It is, however, very remarkable that the word ‘┼Ыr├дddha’ itself does not occur in any undoubtedly authentic and ancient Vedic passage, though the rite called Pi┼Жdapitr yaj├▒a 785 (performed on the am─Бv─Бsy─Б of each month by an

Panegyries of sraddha

great-grandfather is declared to be god V─Бsudeva himself, the one to the grandfather is designated Sankarsana, that to the father is known as Pradyumna and the offerer of the pindas is him self in the position of Aniruddha. In S─Бntiparva 345. 21 it is stated that Visnu should be looked upon as staying in the three pindas. In the K┼лrmapur─Б┼Жa it is stated on the day of Am─Бv─Бsy─Б the pitrs assuming an aerial form come to the door of their former haunt and mark whether ┼Ыr─Бddha is being per formed by men of their family. This they do till sunset. When the sun sets, being oppressed by hunger and thirst, they become full of despair and feel sorrow, breathe heavily for a long time and go away condemning their descendants. The pitrs of him who does not offer sr─Бddha on am─Бv─Бsy├д, even with water or vegetables, go away after cursing him’.

It is necessary to say a few words about the derivation of the word ‘sr├дddha’. That the word is derived from ‘sraddh─Б’ is quite clear. In the definition quoted above from the Brahma pur├дna and the definition 792 given by Marici and Brhaspati the connection of ┼Ыr─Бddha with sraddha is emphasized. In ┼Ыr├дddha one entertains the firm faith or conviction that what is given up to the br─Бhmaс╣Зas for the benefit of the departed man or the Fathers will reach him or them in some way. The Skandapurana VI. 218.3 says that ┼Ыr├дddha is so called because ┼Ыraddh─Б is the root (or main spring) of that rite. This means that there is not only the conviction stated above but that there is a firm belief that a person is under an obligation to offer it. Sraddh─Б is deified and addressed as a deity in Rg. 793 X. 151. 1-5, the first verse of which is explained in the Nirukta (IX, 31). The word also occurs in Rg. II. 26.3, VII. 32. 14, VIII, 1.31, IX. 113. 4. In some verses the two components of the word

sraddh─Б’ (viz. srat’ and ‘dh─Б’) are separated without any change in the meaning. For example, in Rg. II. 12. 5 (= A. V. 20. 34, 5) it is said ‘Have faith in him; O people! he is Indra’. In Rg. X. 147. 1, addressed to Indra, we have I have faith in that high wrath of yours &c.’ (┼Ыratte dadh─Бmi

IVI

A┼Яtak─Б ┼Ыr─Бddha

353

It has already been stated above (pp. 349-350) that in very ancient times there were only three rites for departed ancestors, viz. Pinda-pitr-yaj├▒a (offered by those who had consecrated the srauta fires) or monthly ┼Ъr─Бddha in the case of those who had not done so (vide e. g. A┼бv. Gr. II. 5. 10, Hir. Gr. II. 10. 1, ─Аp. Gr. VIII. 21. 1, Visnupur─Б┼Жa III. 14. 3 &c.), the Mah├дpitr yaj├▒a and the Astak─Б ┼Ыr─Бddhas. The first two have been already described in vol. IL (as said above), but the Astak─Б ┼Ыr─Бddhas have not been described at all so far. Therefore some remarks will be offered here about them. They are of special importance, but the authorities present great variations on almost all points such as the number of days and the months in which they were to be performed, the deities to be worshipped, the offerings to be made and the procedure to be followed.

Gaut. (VIII, 19) mentions ‘Astak─Б’ rite as the first among the seven kinds of p─Бkayaj├▒as and as one of the forty samsk─Бras. Astak─Б appears to have meant the 8th tithi in any month after the Full Moon day (vide Sat. Br. VI. 4. 2.10). The Sat. Br. states 800 ‘On the 8th day (after full moon) he (the performer of agnicayana ) collects the materials for the fire pan, for sacred to Praj─Бpati is the 8th day (after full moon) and sacred to Prajapati is this rite viz. the firepan.’ Sabara in his Bh─Бsya on Jai.801 I.3.cites a verse occurring in the A, V. III, 10. 2 and in the Ap. M. P. II. 20. 27 as a mantra indicative of Astak─Б. The mantra is “May that (Astak─Б) night be very auspicious for us, whom people welcome like a cow coming towards a person and which is the wife of the Year.’ In the A. V. IIL 10. 8 the Ek─Бstak─Б is said to have the year (Samvatsara ) as husband. The Tai. S. VII. 4. 8. 1. provides 802’ Men about to take dik┼Я─Б (consecration) for a Samvatsarasattra should undergo dik┼Я─Б on the Ek─Б┼Яtak─Б; what is called Ek─Бstak─Б is the wife of the year.’ Jai. (VI. 5. 32-37) explains that Ek─Бstak─Б is the 8th tithi after the Full Moon of M─Бgha. The ─Аp. Gr. (quoted by Haradatta

applied to a rite in which the pitrs are the deities worshipped, the greatest divergence prevails as to the devat─Б of the Astak─Бs. The ─А┼Ыv. Gr. (II. 4.3 and II. 5. 3-5) provides that on the 7th of the dark half the offerings are made to the pitrs and on the 9th also, but ─А┼Ыv. Vi┼Ыve-dev─Бh (all the gods ), Agni, S├╝rya, Praj─Бpati, R─Бtri (night), Naksatras (constellations ), the seasons, the Pitrs, Pa┼бus (cattle). The Gobhila Gr. The procedure of Astak─Б comprises three parts, viz. homa, inviting br─Бhmaс╣Зas for dinner (up to seeing them go away after dinner) and the rite called Anvastakya or Anvastak─Б. When the Astak─Бs were deemed to be three or four performed in the several months noted above, all these were gone through at each A┼Яtak─Б. When the Astak─Б rite was performed only in one month i. e, after the Full moon in M─Бgha, the above parts were performed on three days, 7th, 8th and 9th of the dark half. When compressed in one day only, they must have been per formed one after another on the same day.

Many of the Grhyas┼лtras, such as those of ─А┼Ыval─Бyana, Kausika, Gobhila, Hiranyake┼Ыin and Baudh─Бyana describe a very elaborate procedure in the case of Astak─Бs. (the Astak─Б day) the Anvastak─Б rite. Its procedure is explain ed by the description of the monthly ┼Ыr├дddha.

Though ─Аp. Gr. (II. 5.3) and San. Gr. III, 13. 7 state that the Anvastakya rite follows the procedure of Pipdapitryaj├▒a, some Grhyas┼лtras (such as Kh─Гdira III, 5, Gobhila IV. 2-3) give very elaborate descriptions of that rite. The ─А┼Ыv. Gr. and Visnudharmas┼лtra 74 follow a middle course. The description in ─А┼Ыv. Gr. is comparatively brief and it is set out below. It may be noted that some Grhya-s┼лtras state that the Anvastakya rite is performed on the 9th or 10th of the dark half (e. g. Kh─Гdira Gr. III. 5. 1 ’navamim da┼Ыamim v─Бnvastakyam )’. Though some s┼лtras (like ─Ас╗Ыv. Gr. II. 5) declare that the Astak─Б and Anva┼Яtakya are modelled on the monthly ┼Ыr─Бddha or Pindapit┼Яyaj├▒a, others (like the Baud. Gr. III, 12. 1. Gobhila Gr. The Pipda-pitryaj├▒a could be offered on am─Бv─Бsy─Б only by one who was ─Бhit─Бgni (i.e. had kept the sacred vedic fires). It is impossible to believe that everyone became ─Бhit─Бgni. The case was probably the reverse i. e. only a few became ─Бhit─Бgnis and the rest had only the grhya fire or many of the rest were without even the grhya fire. It appears possible that all were required to offer ┼Ыr├дddha on am─Бv─Бsy─Б on the analogy of pindapitryaj├▒a. As the latter became rare, the requirement of offering ┼Ыr─Бddha on am─Гv─Бsv─Б. remained and in the s├╝tras and smrtis all the details were mentioned under m─Бsi┼Ыr─Бddha and in the case of the other gr├дddhas the sutras and smrtis pointed out only what was to be omitted. (II. 5. 2-15) as follows:-Having prepared a portion of the same meat,818 having established the fire on a surface sloping towards the south, having fenced it in and made a door on the north side of the enclosed shed, having strewn round the fire three times sacrificial grass with its roots without touching it, turning the left side (of one’s body) towards the fire, he should place down the things to be offered, boiled rice, boiled rice mixed with sesamum, rice cooked in milk, meal pap with curds and meal pap with honey. The ceremony should follow the ritual of the Pindapitryaj├▒a (vide ─А┼Ыv. ┼Ъr. II. 6). Having sacrificed (part of the foods specified except meal-pap) with honey let him offer portions of those substances to the pitys and to their wives with the addition of liquor and the scum of boiled rice. Some place the portion to be offered into pits, which may be two or six. In those situated to the east he should present the offerings to the pitrs; in those to the west, to the wives. Thereby the cere mony celebrated in the rainy season on the Magh─Б day in the dark fortnight after the full moon of Prausthapada (i. e. Bhadrapada) has been declared. And thus he should offer (a festival like the Anvastak─Б ) to the pitrs every month, obsery ing uneven 819 numbers. He should give food at least to nine (br─Бhmanas) or to any un-even number of brahmanas. (Food should be given) to an even number on auspicious occasions 820

The Anvastakya rite was performed after each of the three or four Astak─Бs and if only one Astaka in M─Бgha were perform ed, then after the 8th of the dark half.

There are two views about the rite called M─Бghy─Бvarsa 821 in ─А┼Ыv. Gr. II, 5.9. Acc. to N─Бr─Бyana, the rite is performed in the dark half of Bh─Бdrapada for three days on 7th, 8th and 9th.822 The other view is that it is a rite like the Astak─Бs but performed on the 13th of the dark half of Bh─Бdrapada, when generally the moon is in the Magh─Б naksutra. There is doubt about the very name of the rite, as the mss. present various forms (vide Oldenberg’s note in S. B. E. vol. 29. p. 103 on S├дn, Gr. III. 13. 1). The real name appears to be M─Бghy─Бvarsa or Magh─Бvar┼Яa (meaning ‘a ┼Ыr─Бddha in the rainy season when the moon is in the Magh─Б nak┼Яatra)’. The Vi┼Яnu Dh, S. 76. 1 823 mentions the following times for offering ┼Ыr─Бddha viz, (twelve) Am─Бv─Бsy─Бs (in a year), the three Astak─Бs, the three Anvastak─Бs, the 13th of the dark half of Bh─Бdrapada when the moon is in the Magh─Б asterism, the seasons of ┼Ыarad and vasanta. In Visnu Dh. S. (78.52-53) also a ┼Ыr─Бddha on the 13th of the dark half of Bh─Бdrapada is highly eulogised. adequate and thorough treatment of all this vast mass would fill a separate volume, but considerations of space forbid such an attempt here. All that can be attempted here at the most (and that too not in all cases) is to present matters chronologi cally i. e. describe how ┼Ыr─Бddha was dealt with in the Samhit─Бs and Br─Бhmaс╣Зa texts, then in the comparatively older Gphya and Dharma s┼лtras, then in such early smftis as those of Manu and Y─Бj., then in some representative Pur─Бpas, then in the early commentaries of Medh─Бtithi, Vij├▒─Бnesvara and Apar─Бrka, and then in the medieval digests. Even in this way only a skeleton of the ceremonies described in some representative work of each class can be exhibited. Many differences of detail which arose owing to lapse of time, the locality, the s─Бkh─Б and usages of each writer, his individual inclination and his ability, will have to be passed over altogether. In the days of the Pur─Бnas the differences in detail in the several s─Бkh─Бs have been adverted to.829a Apart from the smrtis and passages of the Mah─Бbh─Бrata (such as Anus├дsana chap. 87-92) and com mentaries on the S┼лtras, on Manu, Y─Бj. and other smitis, the digests on ┼Ыr─Бddha are legion. Only the following digests (arranged in chronological order) have been laid under contri bution in this volume: Kalpataru on ┼Ыr─Бddha; the H─Бralat─Б and Pitrday it─Б of Aniruddha; the Smrtyarthas─Бra; the Smrticandrik─Б; the Caturvargacintamani (section on ┼Ыr─Бddha) of Hem─Бdri (which in the B. I. edition covers 1716 pages); the ┼Ъr─Бddhaviveka of Rudradhara; the Madanap─Бrij─Бta ; the Sr─Бddhas─Бra (a part of Nrsimhapras─Бda); Sr─Бddhakriya-kaumudi of Govind─Бnanda ; the Sr─Бddhatattva of Raghunandana ; the Sr─Бddhasaukhya (part of Todar─Бnanda); the ┼Ъr─Бddhakalpalat─Б of Vinayaka alias Nandapandita; the Nirnayasindhu; the Sraddhamay├╝kha of Nilakantha; the Sr─Бddhaprak─Б┼Ыa (part of Viramitrodaya); the ┼Ъr─Бddhacandrika of Div├дkarabhatta ; the Smrtimukt─Бphala (on ┼Ыr─Бddha); the Dharmasindhu; the B─Бlambhatti, a commentary on the Mit─Бk┼Яar─Б. While presenting this exhaustive and hetero. geneous material, some generalisations, when called for, will be made here and there. We should now turn to the several matters relating to ┼бr─Бddhas.

First comes the question as to who are entitled to offer sr├дddha (┼Ыr─Бddh─Бdhik├дrin). This matter has been already dealt with in the H. of Dh. vol. III. p. 739 ff., and on page 763 and on pp. 256-261 (notes 581-588) above. It would be noticed that some (like the Visnudharmas┼лtra ) prescribe that whoever takes the wealth of the deceased should offer pindas (i, e. per form ┼Ыr─Бddha for him), while others said that whoever was preferable as entitled to offer pindas to the deceased propositus was to take the wealth. A few matters not mentioned there may be added here. In the Santiparva 65, 13-21 it is narrated830 that emperor M─Бndh─Бtr was told by Indra how Yavanas, Kir─Бtas and similar non-Aryan peoples (that are styled Dasyus in the Epic) are to be made to conduct themselves and it is stated that all dasyus may perform Pitryaj├▒as (in which they should feed men of their own kind and make monetary gifts to them) and offer money to br─Бhmaс╣Зas also. The V─Бyupur─Бna (83. 112) also speaks of the Mlecchas as persons that offer oblations to Pitrs. The general rule is stated by the Gobhila smrti 831 that the husband should not offer pipda to his wife even if she dies sonless, nor a father to his son nor an elder brother to a younger brother. The moral of the story of Ninii who performed ┼Ыr─Бddha for his predeceased son and repented for having done so as it was dharmasankara is the same. Vide Anu┼б─Бsanaparva 91. Apar─Бrka (p. 538) quotes a verse from Sa┼гtrimsan-mata that a father should not perform the ┼Ыr─Бddha of his son nor an elder brother of a younger one. But Brhat par─Б┼Ыara (p. 153) appears to state that even this general rule may have to be set aside sometimes. Baudh─Бyana and Vс╗Кddha┼Ы─Бt─Бtapa (q. by Sm. C, on ┼Ыr├дddha p. 337) allow a ┼Ыr─Бddha (except sapi┼Жdikarana) to be performed by any one for any

IV)

Meaning of ‘putra’

367

has to return only the principal and has to pay no interest and the Mit. quotes a verse of Brhaspati 837 where all the three descendants are mentioned in one breath and the Mit. adds that the great-grandson has not to pay even the principal if he has received no ancestral property. This last remark implies that the Mit, regarded that the great-grandson was also included in the extended sense of ‘putra’. Y─Бj. II. 51 begins by saying that whoever takes the wealth of a deceased person has to pay the latter’s debts, so the great-grandson would have to pay the great-grand-father’s debts if he received the assets of the grand-father. Therefore the Mit. on II. 50 expressly mentions that a great-grandson need not pay his great-grand-father’s debts if he received no assets, because, otherwise being included in the extended meaning of putra, he would have had to pay. There was no necessity to bring in or mention the prapautra under II. 50 if the Mit. did not include the prapautra in the word putra. Again on Y─Бj. II. 51 (‘putrahinasya rikthinaс╕е’) the Mit. included even prapautra under the word putra. This shows that the Mit. is quite conscious that the three descendants of a man form one group and succeed to his estate and liabilities and putra includes three descendants wherever the context so requires. If the word ‘putra’ is not to be taken as only illustrative and as including both grandson and great-grandson, serious difficulties will arise even in the interpretation of Yaj. on which the Mit. comments. For example, in Y─Бj. II. 135-136 it is said that when a gonless man dies his wife, daughters and other heirs (named there ) succeed one after another. If тАШputra’ is taken to mean only son’ and no one else, then on the death of a man without a son his wife or daughter (whoever is alive ) will take the wealth even if a son’s son exists. But that would be absurd and is not stated by any one. Therefore the word putra has to be interpreted in a wider sense in a proper context. Many works such as the Vyavah─Бramayukha, the Viramitrodaya, the Dattakamim─Бng─Б interpret the word ‘putra’ as including three generations. Therefore, though the Mit. in its remarks on inheritance and succession expressly names the son and grand

It is impossible to hold with Dr. Kapadia that the Mit. ran counter to the express dicta of renowned Smrtis such as those of Manu, Sankha-Likhita and Puranas like the Vi┼Яnu-pur├дpa III. 13,30 (quoted above in note 582) and that in its remarks on succession it forgot its own interpretation of putra on Yaj. II. 51. He has also not correctly understood the words of the Mit, introducing Y─Бj. II. 137: ‘sons and grandsons take the wealth; in their absence, the wife and others; thus it is said (by me). This is wrong for several reasons. “Wife and others take the wealth’ is said by Y─Бj. (in II. 135-36). The following words are ’now (the author) declares an exception to both.’ This clearly refers to Y─Бj. (II. 137) and not to Vij├▒─Бne ┼Ыyara and so ‘uktam’ also must refer to Y─Бj. and not to Vij├▒─Бne┼Ыvara. Therefore, according to the Mit, the great-grand son is included in the extended meaning of the word ‘putra’, is entitled just like a son or a grandson to offer ┼Ыr─Бddha (in default of a son or grandson) and to take the wealth and pay the debts of the ancestor. In the matter of payment of debts there is, on account of the difference in the period that elapses, a difference between all the three descendants if no ancestral wealth is left by the ancestor, viz. the son pays the debt with interest, the grandson only the principal lent but without interest and the great-grandson nothing at all. This shows that even between the son and the grandson that are expressly mentioned by Yaj. * II. 50 as to the payment of debts there is a difference and that as the great-grandson had to pay nothing when no ancestral property existed he was not mentioned at all in Y─Бj. Just as the king is an ultimate heir and also the guardian of all minors, so he is like the son of a person (who has no relatives left) for performing ┼Ыr─Бddhas.

The next question is about the times when ┼Ыr─Бddha is to be performed. It has been seen above (vide H, of Dh. vol. II. p. 696 ff) that long before the time of the Sat. Br. five daily observances (called Mah─Бyaj├▒as) were prescribed for each house-holder, viz. the sacrifice to beings, that to men, that to the Fathers, that to the gods and that to Veda. The Sat. Br. and the Tai. ─А. (II. 10) say further that this daily rite in which one offers svadh─Б (food) to the Fathers even up to water was called pitryaj├▒a, Manu III. 70 defines pitryaj├▒a as tarpana (satiating ancestors with the offerings of water). Manu III. 82 provides that an householder should daily perform a sr─Бddha with food or with water or with milk, roots and fruits and thus please the Fathers. Sr─Бddha originally meant a sacrifice performed for the Fathers on Am─Бv─Бsy├д (vide Gaut. 15.1-2).838a By applying that word to the daily oftering of water to the Manes what is intended to be conveyed is that the special characteristics of ┼Ыr├дddha in the strict sense are to be extended to this daily rite so far as possible. Am─Бv─Бsy─Б is of two kinds, Siniv─Бli and Kuh┼л. Those who keep srauta fires should perform ┼Ыr─Бddha on the former, while those who have not kept srauta fires and s├╝dras should offer sraddha on the latter.

Sr─Бddhas are divided into three classes, nitya, naimittika and k─Бmya. An observance is called nitya when it is laid down that it must be performed on a certain or fixed occasion (such as every day, on an am─Бv├дsy├д, or on A┼Яtak─Б day). What is laid down for being done on an occasion which is uncertain is called naimittika (such as the birth of a son). What is ordained to be done in case one desires a certain reward or fruit is called k─Бmya (e.g. the performance of a ┼Ыr─Бddha on Krttik─Б or Rohi┼Жi by one who desires heaven or progeny ). The five daily yaj├▒as including pitr-yaj├▒a are nitya i. e. they must be per formed without any eye to any reward therefrom and the

Passages mentioning the rewards that follow from the performance of obligatory ( nitya ) rites are only laudatory, they only convey that such performances make a man pure, but it is not meant that they are not obligatory and may be performed only if a person desires the rewards or results promised (i, e. such performances are not k─Бmya). ─Аp. Yug─Бdi and Manv─Бdi tithis

Matsya 17. 6-8, Agnipur─Бna 117. 61-64 and 209.16-18, Saura pur├дna 51. 33-36, Padmapur─Бna (Srsti 9. 132-135 ) mention the first tithis of the 14 Manus (or Manyantaras) as follows: 9th of the bright half of ─А┼Ыvina, 12th of the bright half of K─Бrtika, the third of the bright half of Caitra and of Bhadrapada, the am─Бv─Бsy─Б of F├дlguna, the 11th of the bright half of Pausa, 10th of bright half of A┼Я─Бdha and the 7th of the bright half of M─Бgha, the 8th of the dark half of Sr─Бvana, the Full Moon of ─Аs─Бdha, K─Бrtika, Falguna, Caitra and Jyestha. The Matsya pur├дna list is quoted in the Sm. C. I. p. 58, Krtyaratn─Бkara p. 543, Par, M. 1 1. p. 156 and I. 2 p. 311, and the Madanap─Бri j─Бta p. 540. The orders in the Skandapur─Бna VII. 1. 205, 36-39 and the Smrtyarthas─Бra (p. 9) are slightly different. In the Skandapur─Б┼Жa (N─Бgarakhanda) the first tithis of thirty kalpas from Sveta onwards are specified as fit for ┼Ыr─Бddha, but are passed over here.

Ap. Dh. S. II. 842 7. 17. 23-25, Manu III, 280, Vis┼Жu Dh. S. 777.8-9, K┼лrma (II. 16. 3-4), Brahm─Бnda III. 14. 3, Bhavisya I. 185. 1 forbid the performance of ┼Ыr─Бddha at night or at twilight or when the sun has just risen except in the case of an eclipse of the moon, Ap. adds that when once a ┼Ыr├дddha is begun in the afternoon and owing to some cause there is delay and the sun sets then the performer should perform the remaining rites the next day and he should observe a fast till the placing of the pindas on the darbhas. Vis┼Жu Dh. S. declares that ┼Ыr─Бddha performed during an eclipse satisfies the Manes as long as the moon and stars exist and brings to the performer all advantages and the satisfaction of all his desires, while the K┼лrmapur─Б┼Жa threatens that he who would not perform a sraddha in an eclipse sinks (incurs sins or becomes ruined) as a cow in mud. The Mit. on Y─Бj. I. 217 is careful to point ont that though there is a prohibition against eating during the progress of an eclipse of the sun or moon, that prohibition would only affect the eater (the br─Бhmaс╣Зa who eats ┼Ыr├дddha repast in an eclipse) but not the giver who will secure happiness (or good results ) thereby.843

History of Dharma┼Ы─Бstra

[Vol.

Very learned disquisitions are held in Apar─Бrka p. 465 ff, Hem─Бdri p. 313 ff and other writers and digests as to the mean ing of apar─Бhna which is the time for sraddha prescribed by Manu (III. 278). There are several views. Some hold that the part of the day after noon is ‘after-noon.’ The word ‘purv─Бhna’ occurs in Rg. X. 34. 11. Others relying on a ┼Ыruti 844 text

The forenoon is for gods, mid-day for men and afternoon for pit─Ыs’ hold that the third part of the day divided into three parts is ‘apar├дhс╗Нa.’ A third view is that apar─Бhna is the 4th part of the day divided into five parts and they rely 845 on Sat. Br. II. 2.3.9. The five parts are called pratah, saigava, madhyandina (or madhyahna), aparahna and sayahna (or sayam or astagamana). The first three are expressly mentioned even in the Rgveda V. 76. 3. Praj─Бpati-snirti (verses 156-157) says that each of these five parts extends over three muhurtas (the day being divided into fifteen muh┼лrtas). It further states that kutapa is the 8th muh┼лrta from sunrise and that sr├дddha should be begun in kutapa and should not last beyond Rauhina muh┼лrta and that five muhurtas (from 8th to 12th) are the maximum time for ┼Ыr─Бddha, 846 The word kutapa has eight meanings as noted by the Sm. c. (┼Ыr─Бddha) p. 433 and Hem─Бdri on ┼Ыr├дddha p. 320. The word is derived from ku’ meaning ‘condemned’ (i.e.sin) and ’tapa’ means ‘what burns.’ The eight 847 meanings of ‘kutapa’ are ‘midday, a vessel of rhinoceros horn, woollen seat or blanket

from Nepal, silver, darbhas, sesame, cows and daughter’s son.’ The general rule is that sr─Бddhas are performed in the afternoon (but this applies to ┼Ыr─Бddha on New moon, Mah─Бlaya, Astak─Б and Anvastak─Б ┼Ыr├дddhas ), while Vrddhiс║┐r─Бddha and ┼Ыr─Бddha in which only corn is offered (─Бma┼Ыr├дddha) are performed in the morning. Therefore, a man should perform sr─Бddha on holy spots, on river banks, in sacred places and particularly in land belonging to himself, in bowers near hills and on mountain tops.’ The Vi┼Яnudharma-s┼лtra chap. 85 mentions numerous holy places and then adds in these and other tirthas, big rivers, on all natural sandy banks, near streams, on mountains, in bowers, forests, groves and spots that look charming because of being smeared with cowdung ( sraddha may be performed ).’ Sankha (14. 27тАУ29 ) states ‘whatever is given in holy Gay─Б, in Prabh─Бsa, Pu┼Яkara, Pray─Бga, in the Naimisa forest (on the Sarasvati), on the banks of the Ganges, Yamun─Б, Payosni, on Amarakantaka, on Narmad─Б, in Benares, in Kuruksetra, Bhrgutunga, on the Himalaya, on Sapta-Veni, on R┼Яik┼лpa–all that becomes inex haustible.’ The Brahmapur─Бpa ( 220.5-7) also specifies river banks, lakes, mountain tops, sacred spots like Puskara as the proper places for sraddha. The V─Бyupur─Бna, chap. 77 and Matsya 22 contain long lists of sacred places, countries, moun tains in relation to ┼Ыr├дddhas. The Kalpataru (sr├дddha p. 40) and Sr. P. p. 147 state that special characteristics of the tirthas in the several countries that are declared to be fit places for ┼Ыr├дddha should be understood from the inhabitants of those various countries.

Sacred places will be dealt with in a separate section (on tirthas ).

The Vi┼Яnudharmas┼лtra 852 ( chap. 84 ) prescribes that sr├дddha should not be performed in Mleccha country, nor should one go to a Mleccha country and then defines a Mleccha country as one in which the system of the four varnas is not established and states that Ary─Бvarta is beyond that. twelve yojanas in extent and which is to the north of the river Mahanadi and to the south of Kikata (i. e. Magadha ) is not fit for sraddha; similarly the countries called K├дraskara, Kalinga, the country to the north of the river Sindhu and all countries where the system of varnas and ─Б┼Ыramas is not in existence should be sedulously avoided for ┼Ыr├дddhas, The Brahmapur─Бna (220.8-10) makes the somewhat startling remark that the following countries should be avoided for ┼Ыr├дddhas viz, the Kir─Бta country, Kalinga, Konkapa, Krimi (Krivi?), Da┼Ы─Бr┼Жa, Kum├дrya (Cape Comorin), Tangapa, Kratha, the northern banks of the Sindhu river and the south bank of Narmad─Б and the east of the Karatoy─Б.

The Markandeyapur─Б┼Жa 854 prescribes that for a ┼Ыr─Бddha a place (ground) that is full of insects, that is arid, or is burnt by fire, from which proceed sounds that are painful to the ear, that is terrific in its aspect, that emits fetid smell should be avoided.

It was also provided from very early times that certain persons and animals are to be ejected from the place where ┼Ыr─Бddha is to be performed and are not to be allowed to pollute the ┼Ыr─Бddha rite by looking at it or by disturbing it in various other ways. Ap. Dh. Manu (III. 239-242) states: a cand─Бla, a village pig or cock, a dog, a woman in her monthly illness, an impotent person-these should not be allowed to see br─Бhmapas engaged in taking dinner. The classification of Sr─Бddhas. Sraddhas have been variously classified. One classification, viz. into nitya, naimittika and k─Бmya has already been described above (p. 369). Another classification is that into Ekoddista and P─Бrvapa 855. The first is offered to one deceased person alone, while the latter is performed on the am─Бv─Бsy─Б of a month or in the dark half of Bh─Бdrapada or on sankr─Бnti and in it the three paternal ancestors are principally invoked. comes enthusiastic owing to a talk about sraddha or when many learned men gather together at a sacred place and, finding it impossible to have separate cooking arrangements for each, pool their resources for collecting ┼Ыr─Бddha materials and perform simultaneously ┼Ыr─Бddha for the pleasure it affords to themselves and for the gratification of pitrs. The Suddhi ┼Ыr├дddha is one where br─Бhmanas are fed when a person under goes ┼Ыuddhi ( purification) after being guilty of some sin or transgression (it is a subsidiary act in a pr─Бya┼Ыcitta). That sr├дddha is called ‘karm─Бnga’ which is performed at the time of the Garbh─Бdh─Бna rite or at the performance of a soma sacrifice, or at simantonnayana, pumsavana (it is like Vrddhisr─Бddha ). That is called daivika ┼Ыr─Бddha which is intended to propitiate gods ( it is like nityagr├дddha and is performed on the 7th or 12th tithi or the like with sacrificial food). When a man going to a distant country on a pilgrimage or the like performs a sr├дddha in which clarified butter is served ( to br─Бhmapas ) in abundance or when he comes back to his house, that is y─Бtra sr─Бddha. That is called pusti┼Ыr─Бddha which is performed for the health (or fattening ) of the body (when taking some medicine for the purpose ) or for the increase of one’s wealth. Out of these 860 twelve the principal ones are p─Бrvana, ekoddi ┼Яta, vrddhi and sapindana. There are works called ┼Юan-navati-┼Ыr├дddha such as those of Sivabhatta, son of Govinda, and of Raghun─Бtha. Devala went further and recommended that an elaborate ┼Ыr─Бddha may be performed only once a year.

Who should be invited at ┼Ыr─Бddha

who has studied the Veda and is able to teach the whole Veda with its angas, a ┼Ыrotriya–these persons sanctify the company if they eat at a funeral repast. Gaut. 15. 28, Baud. Dh. S. II, 8.2, Manu III. 185-186, Y─Бj. I. 219, Varahapur─Бna 14.2 contain almost the same words about those who sanctify the company of diners (i. e. who are pankti p─Бvana). The Anus─Бsanaparva (90.25-31), K┼лrmapur─Бna II. 21.1-14, Matsya 16. 7-13, Brahmapur─Бna 220. 101-104, V├дyu 79.56-59 and 83.5R-55, Skanda VI. 217. 21-25 give long lists of pankti p─Бvana br─Бhmaс╣Зas. The Hir. Gr. II. 10.2, Baud, Dh. S. II. 2. 7, K┼лrma (II. 21. 14) and others say that a performer of ┼Ыr─Бddha should invite one who is not a relative connected by marriage (such as a maternal uncle) nor one who is of the same gotra, nor one who is connected with the performer by Veda study (i. e. is his teacher or pupil), nor a friend nor one who expects monetary help from the performer. Manu (IIT, 138-139) provides that one should not invite at a ┼Ыr─Бddha dinner a personal friend, that one may gain a friend by making valuable gifts to him (on other occasions), that one should feed at a ┼Ыr─Бddha a br─Бhmana whom he does not deem either his friend or foe and that he who performs sr─Бddhas and offer ings to gods chiefly to gain friends reaps no reward after death by those gr─Бddhas or offerings. But Manu III. 144 (= K┼лrma II, 21-22) provides that one may invite even a friend but not a foe though the latter may be learned. Manu (III. 135-137 and 145-147 ) lays down that the main or best rule to be followed is to present ┼Ыr─Бddha food to those who are devoted to spiritual knowledge, that between a man who has studied one whole recension of the Veda but whose father was not a ┼Ыrotriya and one who is himself not a ┼Ыrotriya but whose father had studied a whole recension of the Veda (i. e.whose father was a ┼Ыrotriya) the latter is the more worthy of the two, that one should strive to feed at a ┼Ыr├дddha an adherent of the Rgveda who has studied one entire recension of that Veda or a follower of the Yajurveda who has studied one Sakh─Б thereof or a singer of s─Бmans who has finished one recension of the S─Бmaveda and that if one of these preceding three is honoured and dines at a ┼Ыr─Бddha, the ancestors of the performer will be gratified up to the seventh generation for a very long time. Harita (q. by Hem─Бdri on gr─Бddha p. 392 and Kalpataru on ┼Ыr. pp. 66-67) describes the qualifications of those who are p─Бnkteya br─Бhmaс╣Зasyiz, they must be born in a high family (possessing four characteri stics), must be endowed with learning ( of six kinds ) and sila

Similar rules are laid down by Visnu Db. S. 83, Brhat-Par─Б┼Ыara p. 150, Vrddha-Gau tama p. 581, Praj─Бpati verses 70-72, Laghu-S├дt─Бtapa verses 99 100, Au┼бanasasmrti (Jiv. vol. I. pp. 523-524). As Medhatithi 864 on Manu III 147 says the gist of all these passages is that a learned br─Бhmana who has studied the Veda, whose conduct is good, whose family is famous, who is the son of a ┼Ыrotriya father and who is not related to the performer must be invited and all the rest is mere arthav─Бda (by way of eulogy). Manu (III. 128) laid down two propositions viz, all food offered as sacrifice to the gods and manes must be given only to a br─Бh mapa who studies the Veda and that whatever is presented to the most worthy br─Бhmaс╣Зa (among br─Бhmaс╣Зas studying the Veda) brings in the greatest rewards. Then Manu (III. 183) declares that panktip─Бvana br─Бhmaс╣Зas are those that sanctify a row of diners among whom sit some who are tainted by (latent) blemishes that make them unfit to be among the diners. Then Manu (III. 184-186) gives examples of panktip─Бvana br─Бh manas viz, those who are the foremost among students of all the Vedas or their expository works and who are born in a family of unbroken descant of Vedic students, who are Trin─Б ciketa &c. Hem─Бdri (on ┼Ыr, pp. 391-395) and Kalpataru (┼Ыr. pp. 64-65) quote numerous verses from Yama on panktip─Бvana.

Manu III, 147 asserts that the best course is to invite a br─Бhmana who fulfils the conditions laid down in Manu III.

But Manu is careful 866 to point out in a later chapter that one who is able to observe the best course, but observes the second best does not reap other-worldly rewards by his actions. Even ─Аp. Dh, S. 867 expressly says that if strangers do not possess the requisite qualifications, then even one’s full brother possessed of all the qualifications (as to Vedic learning, good conduct &c.) and pupils may be fed at a ┼Ыr├дddha. Baud. Dh. S. also allows even a sapi┼Жda to be fed. 868 Gaut. 15. 20 appears to be of the view that even pupils and sagotras may be invited when they are possessed of excellent qualities and strangers with good qualifications are not available. Even in these times very learned br─Бhmanas are un willing to be fed at a ┼Ыr├дddha, particularly within a few years (three or five ) from the death of the person for whose benefit the ┼Ыr─Бddha is to be performed. Smrtis attach a certain stigma to the fact of being the recipient of a ┼Ыr─Бddha dinner and pr─Бya┼Ыcittas are prescribed. For example, the Mit, on Y─Бj. III. 289 quotes several verses of Bh─Бradv─Бja, one of which says “If a br─Бhmana dines at a p─Бrva┼Жa ┼Ыr├дddha he has to perform six pr─Б┼Ж─Бy─Бmas (as expiation), if he dines at a ┼Ыr─Бddha from the third month after a person’s death to one year, he has to undergo a fast; if he dines at a yrddhisr├дddha, he has to per form three pr─Б┼Ж─Бy─Бmas, and a fast for a day and night if he dines at a sapindana ┼Ыr├дddha.’ The Mit. further quotes a

Who should be invited at ┼Ыr─Бddha

389

The Matsyapur─Б┼Жa (16. 11-12) recommends ‘He who expounds (the meaning of) texts; he who enters upon the discussion of ├╛rauta sacrifices and he who knows the rules about the accents of s├дmans is a purifier of panktip─Бvanas; one proficient in the S─Бmaveda, a Vedic student, one endowed with knowledge of the Veda or of Brahma –where these are fed in a ┼Ыr├дddha it yields the highest benefit.’ 871 Though in the above passages the greatest emphasis was laid on the possession of Vedic learning by the brahmanas to be fed, one had also to see whether they were men of good character and observers of the rules of proper conduct, as provided by A┼Ыy, Gr. IV. 7. 2 (note 862), Gaut. 15.9 and Manu II, 118 who says ‘a br─Бlmana 872 knowing only the sacred G─Бyatri but living a well-regulated life is to be preferred and not one who knows the three Vedas but who is not well-regulated in conduct and who eats anything (even forbidden food ) and who is a vendor of everything.’ The Skandapur─Бna VI. 217. 27 recommends that one should make every effort to know the family of the br─Бhmaс╣Зas, then their character (sila), then their age and then the facts about whom they marry or to whom they give their daughters in marriage. The Brahm├д┼Жda (Upodgh─Бta, chap. 15) says that there should be no scrutiny of a br─Бhmana about whom nothing is known because siddhas (yogins) roam about on the earth in the form of br─Бhmaс╣Зas. But if faults in a br─Бhmana are easily seen or if one knows his disqualifica tions on account of one’s dwelling near him, he should not be invited (verses 5-6). The same Pur─Бna (Upodgh─Бta 15. 24-26) arranges the orders of preference as follows: first yati (ascetic), then a br─Бhmaс╣Зa who knows the four Vedas and itih─Бsa, then one who knows three Vedas, then one who knows two, then one who knows one Veda, then one who is an up─Бdhy─Бya. Inquiring into qualifications

391

The Nrsimhapur├дna 878 forbids close inquiry into the character and learning of one who comes by chance as a guest at the time of ┼Ыr─Бddha. That inquiry was allowed as to br─Бhmaс╣Зas who were invited and not as to those who came by chance uninvited as atithis. There are no doubt certain passages particularly in the Puranas where scrutiny into a br├дhmana’s qualifications is condemned. For example, the Skandapur─Б┼Жa quoted by Apa r├дrka (p. 455) and Kalpataru (on ┼Ыr. p. 102) states * The Vedic revelation is that ┼Ыr─Бddha is to be offered to a br─Бhmana) after inquiry (into his learning and character), but straightforward action is better than scrutiny. When one offers sraddha straightforwardly without inquiry his pitrs are gratified and also gods’. The Bhavisyapur─Бpa (q. by Balambhatti ) states ‘it is my view also that one should not test (the qualifications of) br─Бhmaс╣Зas; one should only consider their caste and not their virtues’. Such passages are explained away as referring to a ┼Ыr├дddha at sacred places or as applicable to gifts or to atithis (vide Hem├дdri on ┼Ыr├дddha p. 513, and B├дlambhatti on ─Бc─Бra p. 494 ) 878a

Br├дhma┼Жas were declared to be ap─Бnkteya 879 (not fit to sit in the row of br├дhmana diners or as defiling a row of diners at sr├дddha) on various grounds, such as bodily and mental defects and diseases, pursuit of certain avocations, moral lapses, being guilty of crimes, being followers of unorthodox systems, being inhabitants of certain countries. A distinction has to be made between br─Бhmanas who should not be invited and br─Бhmanas that are ap─Бnkteya or panktid┼л┼Яaka. For example, one should not ordinarily invite a friend or a sagotra br─Бhmaс╣Зa even

Manu III. 170-182 indulge in pointing out how feeding such unworthy br─Бhmanas results in the loss of the gratification of pitrs and state that the food eaten by such unworthy persons becomes or is to be deemed as equal to foul things. The K┼лrmapur─Бna 882 forbids inviting at ┼Ыr─Бddhas Bauddha ascetics, Nirgranthas (devotees who have withdrawn from the world and wander about naked or as beggars), those that follow the Pa├▒car─Бtra and Pasupata doctrines, those that are k─Бp─Бlikas (devotees of Siva of the left hand order) and other similar heretical people. The Vis┼Жupur─Б┼Жa (III. 18. 70 ff) narrates how a king after a bath in a holy place talked with a heretic and had to pass in consequence through the bodies of a dog, a jackal, wolf, vulture, a crow, a crane and peacock and ultimately became freed from the taint by a bath at the ava bhrtha in an A┼Ыvamedha sacrifice. The same Pur─Бna provides (III. 18. 97) that one should avoid talking with or touching heretics, particularly at the time of a religious rite or when one has consecrated for a solemn sacrifice. The V─Бyupur─Б┼Жa 883 provides that people who are ’nagna’ should not be allowed to see a ┼Ыr─Бddha and then defines “nagna’ people as follows: ’the three Vedas are declared to be a protective covering for all beings and therefore those who foolishly abandon the Vedas are called ’nagna’; those who vainly keep matted hair, those who shave their heads for no purpose, those who are nagna (naked) without any cause, those who engage in certain obser vances and mutter certain words aimlessly are called nag n─Бdi’. works as not fit to be invited at a ┼Ыr─Бddha, 894 For example, the Matsyapur─Б┼Жa states that br─Бhmaс╣Зas that are ungrateful, that are atheists, that stay in Mleccha countries or the countries of Trisanku, Karavira, Andhra, Cina, Dravida and Konkana should be carefully avoided at the time of ┼Ыr─Бddha. Hem─Бdri (on ┼Ыr─Бddha p. 505) quotes from the Saurapur─Бna the following: ‘Br─Бhmaс╣Зas hailing from the countries of Anga, Vanga, Kalinga, Saur─Б┼Яtra, (Kathiawar), Gurjara, ─Аbhira, Konkana, Dravida, Daksim─Бpatha, Avanti and Magadha should be avoided at ┼Ыr─Бddhas. It will be noticed that putting the above two passages together, br─Бhmaс╣Зas from half of modern India would have been ineligi ble for being invited at ┼Ыr─Бddhas if these passages were literally followed. This was probably a counsel of perfection prompted by the false pride and prejudices of the authors of those works. The Sr─Бddhaviveka of Rudradhara (pp. 39-41 ) contains one of the longest lists of persons unfit to be invited at a ┼Ыr─Бddha.

The following reason is advanced by the Var─Бhapur─Бna 885 and others for honouring a guest who comes by chance at the time when a ┼Ыr─Бddha rite is in progress: “Yogins wander over the earth assuming different forms that prevent recognition, but doing good to people; therefore a wise man should honour a guest who arrives at the time of the performance of a ┼Ыr─Бddha”. The Bhavisya-pur─Б┼Жa 886 similarly says that an atithi ( guest ) at a ┼Ыr─Бddha is one who comes when least thought of and not one who had arrived before the ┼Ыr─Бddha rite started. The M├дrkandeya ( 26, 30 ) provides that one should not ask such an atithi about his gotra or caraс╣Зa or his Vedic study nor should one consider whether he has a fine appearance. IV]

Honouring atithi at ┼Ыr─Бddha

397

Visnudharmottara and V─Бyu (71.74тАУ75 ) Pur─Бnas that gods, siddhas and yogins wander over the earth in the form of br─Бhmaс╣Зa alithis in order to favour people and to see how sr├дddhas are being performed. About the definition of an atithi and the necessity and mode of honouring a guest in

general, vide H, of Dh. vol. II. pp. 749-756.

Hem─Бdri (Sr─Бddhak─Б┼Жda, pp. 380-385) holds an interest ing discussion as to whether a performer of ┼Ыr├дddha belonging to one recension of a Veda must restrict himself to inviting br├дhmanas that are students of the same recension of the Veda or whether he can invite any br─Бhmana that may have studied any of the three Vedas. Some people relying on a maxim (as in the case of a bride so in the case of an offering’) invite only br─Бhmaс╣Зas of their own s─Бkh─Б possessed of the qualifications above set forth. Hem─Бdri replies that this is a wrong notion, relies on ─Аp. Dh. S. II. 6. 15.9 ‘one should feed 887 in all (religious) acts br─Бhmaс╣Зas that are pure (in their conduct) and that have studied the Veda’ and asserts that no smrti, Itih─Бsa, Pur─Б┼Жa, Gphyas┼лtra nor Kalpas┼лtra contains the restriction of inviting only br─Бhmanas of the performer’s own s─Бkh─Б. He further says that in such texts as ’trin─Бciketas trimadhuh’ (quoted in note 862a above) the rule laid down is to invite br─Бhmaс╣Зas that have studied different sakh─Бs and Vedas. He rejects the idea about any restriction as to selecting a bridegroom of the same s─Бkh─Б as the bride’s father and remarks that if some people are not prepared to give their daughters in marriage to young men belonging to other ┼Ы─Бkh─Бs, that is due to ignorance about the families and is also due to pride and vanity. He winds up by saying that in Aryavarta countries it is found on all sides that marriage connections are entered into with persons studying different s─Бkh─Бs but living in the same district, (such connections) not being con demned, while persons who study the same s─Бkh─Б of the Veda but do not know each other do not enter into marital connec tions.888 As a contrast to this commonsense view it should be

Yati preferred as an invitee

ing (of food ) is eaten by a yati that knows the truth about pralcrti (primordial matter) and the gunas (sattva, rajas and tamas) reaps the reward (merit) of feeding a thousand (other brahmanas). Therefore one should feed in offerings to gods and manes an excellent yogin who is intent on true knowledge of God and others only if such a one is not available.’ Similar verses about ascetics and yogins occur in Varahapurana 14.50, Skanda (VI.217.7 ff) and Vayupuranas91 chap.71.65-73, chap.76.28 &c. Brhaspati provides 892 a special rule that, if a person cannot afford to feed at a ┼Ыr─Бddha more than one br─Бhmaс╣Зa, then he should feed one who has studied the S─Бmaveda, since in him all the three viz. Rks, the Yajus and Samans co-exist, that the father is pleased by Rks (i. e. by the feeding of a brahmana who has studied the Rgveda), the grand-father by Yajus, the great-grand-father by a S─Бman and a chandoga (a chanter of the whole of Samaveda) is superior. A verse of Satatapa is 893 quoted to the effect that if a student of the Atharvaveda is fed in a rite for the gods or manes, that yields endless and inex haustible rewards.

Some of the smс╗Щtis were very strict in laying down the qualifications of br─Бhmaс╣Зas to be invited at a ┼Ыr─Бddha. Ausa nasa (chap. 4) asserts: ’that br─Бhmaс╣Зa 891 is called durbr─Бh mana and should never be invited at a ┼Ыr─Бddha in whose family Veda study and Vedi (i. e, the performance of Srauta sacri fices) have been stopped for three generations’. author 895 further says that six persons are merely brahma bamdhus (i. e. brahmanas by birth or caste alone) viz. one who is hired by a s┼лdra or a king as a servant, who has a s┼лdra woman as his wife, who is a village priest and he who subsists by killing (animals) or by catching them. So early as the Mah─Бbh─Бsya 896 it was stated that austerities (leading a life of restraint and strict observances), Vedic learning and birth (from brahmana parents) are the causes of (a man being called) a br─Бhmaс╣Зa and that he who is devoid of the first two is a mere br─Бhmaс╣Зa by caste (but not a real br─Бhmana). It is curious to note that Yama stated that, if br─Бhmaс╣Зas that do not declare (or point out) the auspicious nak┼Яatra or tithi or day or mu h┼лrta and other auspicious matters, eat (┼Ыr─Бddha) food it be comes inexhaustible.

But the requisite qualifications were so exacting that it must have been found almost impossible to secure for a ┼Ыr─Бddha br─Бhmaс╣Зas altogether free from any of the blemishes set out above from Manu. Gautama (15. 15-18) contains long lists 897 of over 50 kinds of br─Бhmanas that were not to be invited at a ┼Ыr─Бddha dinner or at a sacrifice for gods, but Gaut, adds that according to some only those beginning with ‘durv─Бla’ (Gaut. in 15.18) were to be shunned at a ┼Ыr─Бddha (but could be invited at a sacrifice for the gods). Persons to be shunned

leprosy, the son of a re-married woman, a gambler, one who neglects japa ( the recitation of Vedic mantras), a servant of the king, one who uses false weights and measures, one whose (only) wife is a s├╝dra female, one who does not perform the daily five sacrifices, one who suffers from a virulent skin disease, a usurer, one who lives by trade or by handicrafts, one who makes his living by (manufacturing) bows (and arrows) or by playing on musical instruments or by keeping time (when another is singing), or by dancing or singing. inviting learned and well-conducted br─Бhmaс╣Зas for ┼Ыr─Бddha. The idea (expressed by Manu III. 189 and the Padmapur─Б┼Жa) persists that the pitrs enter into and hover round the invited br─Бhmanas and that the latter are to be looked upon as represen ting the pitrs.899 The Garudapur─Бna states that Yama allows the departed souls and the pitrs to visit the world of men at the time of sraddha from the nether regions.

The Visnu Dh. S. (79.19-21) prescribes that the performer should avoid wrath, should not shed tears and should not do things in a hurry. K┼лrma (uttar─Бrdha 22.8) states that if a person first invites a br─Бhmana and then foolishly invites another (passing over the first) then he becomes a greater sinner (than the br─Бhmana who after accepting one invitation promises to dine at another ┼Ыr─Бddha) and is born as a worm in human faeces. The Bhavisyapurana. 902 provides that honouring gods, pitrs and men and feeding (br─Бhmaс╣Зas) should not be done without wearing an upper garment; otherwise the rite will bear no fruit.

About the number of br─Бhmaс╣Зas to be invited at a ┼Ыr─Бddha there were several options and several views. The ─Аsv. Gr. S. states 903 that at the P─Бrvana-┼Ыr─Бddha (performed on a parvan day i. e. on Amavasya), the Abhyudayika sraddha, the Ekod dista or K─Бmya, the larger the number of br─Бhmaс╣Зas the greater is the reward, that in no case should a person invite only one br├дhma┼Жa at a ┼Ыr─Бddha meant for all pitrs or he may optionally invite only one br─Бhmaс╣Зa except at the first ┼Ыr─Бddha, that he may invite one, two or three br─Бhmaс╣Зas for each of the three paternal ancestors. The S─Бn. Gr. (IV. 1,2) and Kausitaki Gr. III. 14.1-2prescribe that one should 904 invite an uneven number of br─Бhmanas, at least three, to sit down as (representing the ) fathers. of brahmanas, at least nine or as many as he is able (to food) and that they should be learned in the Veda and endowed with polished speech, good appearance, mature age and good character’. If five were invited two would be for gods and three for pitrs; if soven, then four for gods and three for pitrs and so on. Vas. XI. 27 ( = Manu III, 125 = Baud. Dh. S. II. 8. 29), Y─Бj. I. 228, Matsya 17. 13-14, Visnupur─Бna III. 15.14 provide that one must feed two br─Бhmanas at the rite for the gods and three for the manes or one only for each of the two purposes and even a rich man should not go in for a large company. The Padma pur─Б┼Жa (Srsti 9.98 and 141) says the same thing. So the number of br─Бhmanas to be invited did not depend so much upon the means of the inviter, but upon the point whether the inviter would be able to honour them all properly and with ease. The idea was that at the same time when ┼Ыr─Бddha was to be performed two br─Бhmanas should be fed for gods and three for the pitrs. When only one br─Бhmana could be invited or was available, Vas. The result is that if a man can afford to invite only one br─Бhmana or can secure one only, then that br─Бhmaс╣Зa is meant for the rite in honour of pitrs and the offering for the gods is to be cast into fire. The K┼лrmapur─Бna (uttar─Бrdha 92.32) insists that an atithi must be fed at a sraddha or other-. wise the ┼Ыr─Бddha is not praiseworthy. Though these ancient works insisted upon the avoidance of large preparations and expenses for ┼Ыr─Бddhas in honour of a deceased person, there were other smrtis that favoured lavish distribution of wealth in sr─Бddhas. For exan─▒ple, Brhaspati lays down:

( An heir ) should lay aside half of the wealth that comes to him (by inheritance ) for the benefit of the deceased owner and should expend it in the monthly, six-monthly and yearly ┼Ыr─Бddhas’. The D─Бyabh─Бga XI. 12 approves 908 of this and also guotes Ap. Dh. S. II. 6.13.3 “On the failure of a sapinda the teacher of the Veda takes the wealth of the deceased, on failure of the teacher, the pupil takes it and having inleri ted it he should employ it in the performance of works of charity for the benefit of the deceased’ (or he himself may enjoy it). These passages show to what lengths the cult of benefit to the soul of the deceased was carried in India by certain writers. More practical authors such as Haradatta did not relish these extreme views. In several pur─Бnas such as the V─Бvu 908a and Visnu there are express directions that when a ┼Ыr─Бddha is performed at Gay─Б, it should be on a profuse scale and no stinginess 909 (lit. cheating in money matters ) in spending wealth should be shown there; otherwise the performer would not reap the benefit of the performance of ┼Ыr─Бddha at that holy place. Lavish expenditure recommended

expenditure of wealth in all ┼Ыr─Бddhas. The V─Бyupur─Б┼Жa 910 (82. 26-28 ) further says that the br─Бhmanas of Gay─Б are super men, that when they are gratified (at a ┼Ыr─Бddha) the gods together with pitrs become gratified, that no question should be raised about the family, the character, the learning and the austerities (of the Gay─Б br─Бhmaс╣Зas), that by honouring them a man attains liberation, that a man after honouring the br─Бhmaс╣Зas should proceed according to his resources and strength to the performance of ┼Ыr─Бddha; thereby he secures all heavenly desires and obtains the means of Moksa. The Skanda pur─Бna goes so far as to say that Gay─Б br─Бhmaс╣Зas even if they are depraved in their conduct and are backward deserve to be invited at ┼Ыr├дddha and are superior to br─Бhmanas who have mastered the Veda and Ved─Бngas. The Nirnayasindhu (III. p. 401 ) notes that, according to the Tristhalisetu of his grandfather, this provision holds good only in the case of the ┼Ыr─Бddha at the Aksayya Vata in Gaya and nowhere else. In modern times the br─Бhmanas at Gay─Б used to require the performer of ┼Ыr─Бddha while he was in the sacred Phalgu river to make a declaration about his wealth and demanded fees accordingly, thereby carrying to the letter the words of the V─Бyupur─Бna. Many people returned from Gay─Б thoroughly dis illusioned and disgusted with the conduct of the br─Бhmanas at Gay─Б. In the Var─Бhapur─Бna 911 it is said that two verses were sung by the pitrs viz.Would such a blessed and intelli. gent man be born in our family who will offer pindas (i. e. ┼Ыr─Бddha) to us without being stingy about wealth and who would bestow on br─Бhmaс╣Зas with reference to us (i. e. for our b╔Щnefit) jewels, clothes, land, costly vehicles and all other kinds of wealth including water, when he has riches enough? Here lavish expenditure on all ┼Ыr─Бddhas (not only at Gay─Б. ┼Ыr─Бddha) appears to be strongly recommended. Devala prc

The Matsyapur─Б┼Жa 913 and Padma (S╚Щsti-khanda 9.85-88) provide that the person intending to perform a ┼Ыr─Бddha should in an humble manner invite the br─Бhmanas on the previous day or (in the morning of the day of ┼Ыr─Бddha, that he should touch the right knee (of the br─Бhmana to be invited) with the words ‘you are given this invitation by me’ and repeat in their hearing the following observance you should be free from anger, should be intent on purity of body and mind) and should abstain from sexual intercourse and I, the performer of ┼Ыr─Бddha, shall also act in the same way and that the pitrs in an aerial form wait upon the invited br─Бhmanas,’ The Brhan-n─Бrad─лya-pur─Бna states that the invitation should be in the words ‘O best men! History of Dharma┼Ы─Бstra

[Vol.

there is a conflict among smrtis and the medieval digests propose an option (vide Hem─Бdri on ┼Ыr─Бddha pp. 1154-1157). Manu III. 205 appears to lay down that the daiva br─Бhmana should be invited first (daiv─Бdyantam tad-iheta). Yama quoted by several digests 915 says that the performer should request in the evening of the previous day br─Бhmaс╣Зas with the words You should all be free from exertions and should avoid passion and anger for the ┼Ыr─Бddha in my house which is to be performed tomorrow,’ that the br─Бhmaс╣Зas should reply ’let it be so if the night passes happily and without any mishap to us! digests (e. g. ┼Ъr─Бddhakriy─Бkaumudi p. 81, ┼Ъr─Бddhatattva p. 194 and Nirnayasindhu III, p. 804) say that the verse ‘sary─Бy─Бsa &c,’ may be repeated when the invitation is given on the day previous to the day of ┼Ыr─Бddha and the verse ‘akrodhanaih’ when the invitation is given on the morning of the ┼Ыr─Бddha day. The words of invitation differ according to different authorities, For example, according to the Mit. on Y─Бj. I. 225 the words are ┼Ыr─Бddhe ksanah kriyat─Бm.’. Vide Sr. Pr. p. 106 also, Manu III. 187 and 191 show that the words ’nimantrana’ and ‘amantrana’ are used as synonyms. In the Sr─Бddhas┼лtra 916 of K─Бty─Бyana the word ‘─Бmantrana’ is used. But P─Бnini 917 (III. 3. 161) apparently makes a difference between the meanings of the two words and the Mah─Бbh─Бsya explains that invitation is called ’nimantrana’ which if rejected (without proper cause) involves a fault or sin, while that invitation which one is free to reject (without incurring blame) is called ‘─Бmantrana.’ There fore, it must be held that the few writers such as K├дty─Бyana who employ amantrana use it in a secondary sense. The invitation should be given by a performer himself or by his son,

Mode of inviting a br─Бhmaс╣Зa

409

brother or a pupil or a br─Бhmaс╣Зa, but it should not be given through a person of another varna 918 or a woman or a child or person belonging to another gotra nor from a distance (Praj─Бpati 64). Pracetas provides that a br─Бhmana performer of gr─Бddha when giving an invitation should touch the right knee, a ksatriya inviter the left knee of the invitee, a Vaisya inviter should hold both feet of the invitee and a s┼лdra should prostrate himself at the feet of the invitee (vide Sr. Pr. p. 106 and S. The Markandeya (28. 35) states an exception that if, when a ┼Ыr─Бddha rite is going on, br─Бhmaс╣Зas or Vedic students or ascetics come by chance begging for food, the performer should make them pleased by falling at their feet and feed them (i.e. no formal invitation is necessary in these cases). Vide Visnupur├дna III. 15. 12 for feeding uninvited ascetics. It is provided by Bhrgu quoted by Hem─Бdri that the br─Бhmaс╣Зas on accepting the invitation should pronounce the finely-worded and comprehensive Vedic benediction quoted below.919

U┼бanas 919a provides that the performer should wash the floor of his house with water, cowdung it and cleanse the vessels on the day previous to the ┼Ыr─Бddha and then give an invitation to the br─Бhmanas with the words tomorrow I am going to perform ┼Ыr├дddha’. The Var─Бhapurama and the Kurma also provide for this and for the washing of the clothes. Manu III. 206 also requires that the spot where ┼Ыr├дddha is to be performed should be clean, secluded, cowdunged and should slope to the south.
