mana who has been invited (to a ┼Ыr─Бddha dinner) by a faultless performer should not refuse the invitation nor should he, after being invited (and having accepted the invitation), accept a gift of even (uncooked) food from another person. Manu III. 190 and K┼лrmapur─Бna provide that if a br─Бhmana after receiving an invitation for a sacrifice to gods or manes according to ┼Ы├дstra directions and after having accepted it violates the appoint ment, he incurs sin and becomes a hog 921 (in his next birth). This does not apply where he is unable to go on account of illness or other valid reason,

The smrtis laid down some strict and elaborate rules which were to be observed by the br─Бhmaс╣Зas invited for ┼Ыr─Бddha and by the performer himself. Many of the rules are applicable to both. Gaut. prescribes 922 that the br├дhmana who has partaken of ┼Ыr─Бddha dinner should remain chaste (i. e. shun sexual inter course) that whole day, and if he has intercourse with a wife of the s┼лdra caste he thereby makes his own pitrs stay in the ordure of that wife. Vas. XI, 37 makes this rule applicable both to the performer and the invited br─Бhmaс╣Зa and as regards wives of all var┼Жas. Manu III. 188 provides that the br─Бhmana invited to dine at a sacrifice in honour of pitrs and the per former of the ┼Ыr─Бddha should remain controlled (i. e. chaste and free from anger and passion) and should not study the Veda (except japa). Y─Бj. I. 225 (latter half) briefly puts the matter by saying ’they should be controlled as to their bodies, speech and thoughts’. The Matsyapurana 923 prescribes that both the performer of ┼Ыr─Бddha and the br─Бhmana invited to dine at it should avoid dining again (after the ┼Ыr─Бddha dinner), journey, going in a conveyance, exertions, sexual intercourse, study of the Veda, quarrel and sleeping by day. Rules for performer and invitee

411

┼Ыr─Бddha and also on the previous day if invitation be given on the day previous to the gr─Бddha day. Vide Visnu Dh. S. 69. 2-4, The Mit, on Y─Бj. Au┼бanasa (Jiv. vol. I. pp. 526-527) contains verses very similar in import to K─Бty─Бyana. Laghu-Sankha 29, Laghu-H─Бr─лta 75 and Likhita 60 have the same verse requiring the invited brahmanas to avoid eight matters, viz. dining again, journey, carrying loads, Vedic study, sexual intercourse, making gifts, accepting gifts, performing homa, while Praj─Бpati 92 substi tutes the brushing of the teeth (with a twig), t─Бmbula, bath after applying oil to the body, and fast for the first four of the above eight. The Anu┼б─Бsanaparva (90. 12-13) and Padma (P─Бt─Бlakhanda 101. 94-95) also contain a list of actions that should be avoided. Briefly put, the following were the obser vances for both inviter and invitee, viz. avoidance of sexual intercourse, dining again, falsehood, hurry, vedic study, heavy work, gambling, carrying burdens, giving gifts and acceptance of gifts, theft, journey, sleep by day, quarrels; the performer alone was to abstain from eating tamb┼лla, shaving, applying oil to the body, brushing the teeth with a twig; while the br├дh.

mana invited was (alone) to observe the following, viz. not absenting oneself after accepting an invitation, making no delay when called for dinner (vide Sr─Бddhakalik─Б folio 4b and 5a and Pitr-bhakti on ┼Ыr─Бddha 926 ).

Elaborate provisions are made from ancient times about the substances and utensils proper for being used at sr─Бddha and about those that should not be used therein. Ap. Dh. 927 S. remarks: the materials in ┼Ыr─Бddha are sesamum, m─Бsas, rice, yavas (barley ), water, roots and fruits; but the pitrs are extremely gratified by food that is mixed with clarified butter and for a very long time; so also they are gratified by wealth that is obtained lawfully and is bestowed on worthy persons’. Manu III. 267 ( V─Бyu 83.3) is to the same effect as Ap. Dh. S. Y─Бj. I. 258 is content to say that food which is fit to be offered in sacrifices (havisya) should be served. Manu III, 257 explains that food eaten by hermits in the forest, (cow’s) milk, soma juice, meat that is not prepared with spices (or that is free from a bad smell), rock salt are by their very nature havis (sacrificial food). According to Gaut. 27. 11 the sacrificial food (havis) comprises boiled rice, food obtained by begging, ground barley (after being baked or fried), grain separated from husk, barley gruel, vege tables, milk, curds, clarified butter, roots, fruits and water. 928 Other smrtis and digests very much elaborated these brief indications in the early works. The three kinds of wealth (viz. ┼Ыukla, sabala and krsna ) and the several lawful or uncondemned means of acquiring wealth have been described already in H. of Dh. vol. II. pp. 130 ff. The M─Бrkandeya (29. 14-15) condemns the use in ┼Ыr─Бddhas of wealth that is obtained by taking bribes or from a patita (one guilty of a grave sin), that springs from bride-price or that is declared to be unlawful or is obtained by saying to another ‘give me for the sake of a ┼Ыr─Бddha to be offered to my father’ (q. by Sm.C. on

IV)

What milk and water to be used

415

From considerations of space this matter cannot be pursued further. The Mit, on Y─Бj. I. 240 puts together a long list of allowed and of condemned kinds of grains and other articles.

What milk should be ordinarily partaken of and what should be avoided has been dealt with in H. of Dh, vol. II, pp. 782-783. A few words are added here. Manu III, 271 and Y─Бj. I. 258 provide that if cow’s milk or rice cooked therein (called p─Бyasa) is offered in sr─Бddha the pitrs are satisfied for one year. V─Бyu 78. 17, Brahma 935 220.169, M├дrkandeya 32,17-19, Vi┼Яnupur─Бna III.16.11 forbid the use in a ┼Ыr─Бddha of the milk of a she-buffalo, of a camari or female deer, of sheep or ewes, of she camels, of human females and of all animals with one hoof and the use of the curds and clarified butter prepared from such milk. But ghee prepared from buftalo milk was allowed by Sumantu and Devala (q. by Hem─Бdri on ┼Ыr─Бddha p. 572).

The M├дrkandeyapur─Бna 936 (29.15-17), V─Бyu (78.16) and Vi┼Яnupur─Бpa (III, 16.10) lay down that the water to be employed in sraddha must not have a bad smell, must not be foamy, or taken from a puddle or a small reservoir which cannot slake the thirst of a cow, must not have been brought overnight, must not be taken from a reservoir not dedicated to all or from a trough or the like meant for beasts.

Several rules are laid down about the fruits, roots and vegetables recommended or condemned for use in sr─Бddha. For example, the Brahma-pur─Б┼Жa (220.156-158 ) enumerates several kinds of fruits such as mangoes, bilva, pomegranate, cocoanut, dates, grapes, as fit to be given in ┼Ыr├дddha. Vide Sankha 14.22-23 also. V─Бyu (78.11-15 ) states936c that garlic, leeks and onions, other things that are of bad odour or taste

and all exudation from trees not permitted by the Veda and salt gathered from saltish earth, should be avoided in ┼Ыr─Бddha. The Vi┼Яnudharmas┼лtra 937 (79.17) contains a long list of fruits, bulbs and vegetables that were not to be employed in sraddha. The R─Бm─Бy─Бna states 938 that R─Бma when an exile in the Dandaka forest gratified his pitys by offering the fruits of inguda, badara, and bilva trees and generalises that deities are offered that food which is partaken of by a person (who is a devotee of That deity). From considerations of space detailed references to the smс╗Щtis and pur─Б┼Жas are passed over. The Smс╗Щtyarthas├дra pp. 52-53, Sr─Бddhaviveka (pp. 43-47 ) of Rudradhara and other digests collect in one place the foods, vegetables, fruits and roots that are allowed to be offered in ┼Ыr─Бddha and that are condemned in sraddha. Manufactured salt was forbidden, but natural salt from a lake (called saindhava) was allowed. Salt was not to be served directly (as Visnudharmas┼лtra 79.12 says) but when put in while cooking vegetables it was not prohibited. There was a difference of opinion about the employment of asafoetida (vide Hem─Бdri on Sr─Бddha p. 565). The Visnudharmasutra (79.5-6) provides that flowers having a strong (or nasty) odour or no odour at all, the blossoms of thorny plants and red flowers should not be given, but one may give white and sweet-smell ing flowers even though they are taken from thorny plants and flowers though red in colour may be taken from aquatic plants. Sankha (14. 15-16) is to the same effect (q. by Hem─Бdri p. 684). V├дyu (75. 33-35) is to the same effect and adds that the flowers called Jap─Б, Bhandi, R┼лpik─Б (of arka plant), Kurantaka should be avoided in sraddha. The Brahmapurana (220.162 165 ) specifies the several kinds of flowers that may be offered in ┼Ыr─Бddha such as j─Бti, campaka, mallik─Б, mango blossom, tulasi, tagara, ketaki and various kinds of lotuses ( white, blue and red &c.). History of Dharma┼Ы─Бstra

greenish darbhas together with ends uncut, that are smooth and well nourished, one aratni in length and touched with that part of the hand called pitrtirtha are pure, The Padmapur─Б┼Жa (Srstikhanda 11.92 ) and Skanda VII1. 205.16 state that ku─гas and black sesamum spring from the body of Visnu and the Vispudharmottara I. 139.12 says that tilas and darbhas sprang from the perspiration and hair of Visnu in the Boar incarna tion. The Matsya ( 22.89 ) says the same.

The Garuda 941 (Pretakhanda 2.21-22) states that all the three gods dwell in kusa grass viz. Brahm─Б at its root, Visnu in the middle and Sankara at the end and that br─Бhmaс╣Зas, mantras, ku┼Ыas, fire, tulas─▒ leaf–these do not become nirm─Бlya (stale and so unfit to be used again ) even when the same are employed again and again. But an exception is made by Gobhila 942 that those darbhas which are spread on the ground for placing pindas on them or that are used in tarpana and those that are held in the hand while a man is answering the calls of nature should be given up (and not used again). The Vis┼Жu Dh, S. 79.2 and V├дyu 75.41 provide that if ku┼бas are not avail able, k─Б┼Ыa grass or D┼лrv─Б may be substituted. The Skanda pur─Бna VII (Prabh─Бsakhanda ) part 1.206.17 says that straight darbhas are used in giving gifts, at baths, in japa, homa, dinner and worship of gods, but they are double-folded when used in rites for pitrs. The Skanda VII. 1. 205,16 provides that the top of darbhas is for divine rites, while darbha with the root and tip is meant for paityka rites. This is based on the Sat. Br. II. 4. 2.17 which states that the top of the darbha belongs to gods, the middle to men and the root part to the fathers,

Great importance was attached to the use of tila (sesamum) in ┼Ыr├дddha. The Jaiminigshya II.1 states that the whole house should have sesamum grains scattered about in it. Baud. Dh. S. II. 8,8 provides that when the invited brahmanas come they should be given water mixed with sesame. The Baud. gr. II. 11.64 provides that sesamum grains are holy in sraddha for making gifts of them or as part of food or for being mixed in

The Prajapatismrti speaks 943 of four kinds of tilas viz. white, black, very black and jartilas and states that each succeeding one gives greater gratification to the pitrs than each preceding one. The Tai.s.V. 4.3.2 refers tojartilas and Jai. X.8.7 holds a discussion thereon. The Naradapurana (purvardha 28.36) 944 provides that the performer of ┼Ыr─Бddha should scatter tilas in the midst of the br─Бhmaс╣Зas invited and at the doors with the mantra ‘apahat─Б’ (may the asuras and evil spirits that sit on the altar be struck and run away). Yaj. I. 234 also recommends this mantra ( which is V─Бj. S. II. 29). The K┼лrma purana (II. 22.18) states that sesame should be scattered all round and a goat should be tied near the spot, since sr─Бddha polluted by asuras becomes purified by sesame and a goat. The Visnupur─Бna (III. 16.14) prescribes that by tilas scattered on the ground one should ward off evil spirits (Y─Бtudh─Бna ). The Garudapurana 945 ( Pretakhanda 2. 16 ) makes Srikrsna say “tilas have sprung from the perspiration on my body and are holy; asuras, d─Бnavas and daityas run away on account of tilas.’ The Anus─Бsana-parva (90.22 ) says that y─Бtudh─Бnas and goblins snatch away the havis when the sr─Бddha is offered without tilas. The Vayu (74. 1-2), Matsya (17. 19-22), Brahm─Бnda (Upodgh─Бta 11. 1-2) and Padma (Srstikhanda 9. 147-150) state that vessels of gold, silver or copper are the (proper) ones for pitrs; that even the talk about silver or the sight or gift of silver gives inexhaustible results to pitrs in heaven, that vessels to be used for arghya, for pipda and for the food to be offered should be preferably of silver and that in rites for gods a silver vessel is not auspicious. Atri (q. by Sm. C. S. 79.22 and 24). The Padma provides 947 that the vessels may be of sacrificial wood or of pal─Б┼Ыa or of silver or made from a sea product (such as conch shell) and that since silver was produced from the eye of Siva, it is a great favourite with pitrs. Serving flesh at ┼Ыr─Бddha

423

fish called ‘satabali’ and the flesh of a V─Бrddhr─лnasa. Vas. XI. 34 contains the following remarkable Verse: ‘an ascetic, when invited in a rite for the gods or pitrs, who avoids (does not partake of) flesh, dwells in Hell for as many years as the number of hair (on the body of the animal whose flesh he avoids).’ Even the Visnudharmottarapur─Бna (T. 140. 49тАУ50) emphatically asserts that he who does not partake of flesh-food in a row of diners at a gr─Бddha which has been properly em ployed goes to hell Manu V. 35 and K┼лrma II. 17.40 contain a similar verse applicable to all those who are invited as br─Бh ma┼Жas at a ┼Ыr─Бddha. The K┼лrmapur─Б┼Жa II. 22.75 provides that the brahmana who is employed for the performance of a ┼Ыr├дddha and does not eat flesh offered therein becomes a beast for 21 births. Manu III. 257 states that the following are said to be proper offerings in a ┼Ыr─Бddha by their very nature viz. food (prepared from n─лv─Бra grain and the like) fit for a forest hermit, milk, soma juice, flesh that does not emit foul smell and unmanufactured salt. An ascetic was ordinarly required not to partake of flesh; but Vasistha insisted on his partaking of it when invited at a ┼Ыr─Бddha.

Manu IIT. 267-272, Y─Бj. I. 258тАУ260, Visnu Dh. The verses of Y─Бj. being the shortest in all these works are given below. There is some divergence of views among the several works. For example, Manu III. 267 and 271, Katy─Бyana (in sr─Бddhas┼лtra 7 ) appear to hold that by offering food prepared from village corn (such as rice, m─Бsa & c.) or wild eatables (such as n─лv─Бra or fruits and roots) the gratification is only for one month and the flesh of V─Бrdhrinasa produces gratification for twelve years only (and not for all time ). Hem─Бdri (on ┼Ыr├дddha p. 590 ) 953 is careful to point out that these words about the duration of time are not to be taken literally but what is really intended is to convey greater and greater gratification of the pitrs according to the kind of flesh offered. IV)

Use of flesh in modern times

425

securing their favour. In course of time that conception grew 361 onger and stronger, so much so that Manu (V. 27-44 and V.46-47) and Vasistha appear to be in two minds (vide H. of Dh. vol. II pp. 778тАУ780). Gradually the offering of flesh in Madhuparka and in ┼Ыr─Бddhas came to be totally condemned in works of the 12th and 13th centuries and onwards as a matter prohibited in the Kali age (Var─Бtithipitrbhyasca pa┼б┼лp─Бkaranakriya). (Vide H. of Dh, vol. III pp. 945-946 and p. 964). Now except among the br─Бhmanas (in Northern India ) who have no objection to include fish in diet as permissible to them no br─Бhmana offers flesh in ┼Ыr─Бddha, The usage of Northern India would be in accordance with the view set out in Brhann─Бradiya-pur─Бna that one should offer honey, flesh and other things according to the usage of the country, as explained by the P┼Щthvicandrodaya.

Manu ( V.11-18) contains long lists of animals, birds and fishes whose flesh was not to be eaten even by those who were flesh-eaters.

If a person is destitute, some of the Pur─Бс╣Зas such as the Visnu (III. 4.24-30) and the Var─Бha (13,53-58) mercifully provide in identical 955 verses that instead of entertaining br─Бhmanas with a sumptuous dinner or flesh the poor man may offer only un cooked corn, or some vegetables growing wildly or some slight daksin─Б if he cannot offer even uncooked food or vegetables, or he may offer a few grains of sesamum (7 or 8 ) to a br─Бhmana with water in his folded hands, or grass to a cow enough for one day and if he cannot afford even any one of these, then he may repair to a thicket of trees, raise his arms so that his armpits are exposed and loudly address the guardians of the worlds such as the Sun in the following words: ‘I have neither wealth nor money nor anything else fit to be offered by way of ┼Ыr─Бddha; I bow to my pitrs; may the pit┼Щs be satisfied by my devotion; I have stretched these arms in space!’ (lit, the path of the wind).

It is now time to describe the procedure of the P─Бrva┼Жa Sraddha. 955a which is the pattern or norm (prakrti) of the other ┼Ыr─Бddhas 956 (even including the A┼Яtak─Бs). Here one meets with great divergences of views even from the times of the s┼лtras up to modern times. Though the main items and stages in the rite of ┼Ыr─Бddha are generally the same, there is variation in the mantras, the details and sometimes in the order of the several items. K─Бty─Бyana lays down that every man has to follow his own s┼лtra as to the use of the word ‘sv─Бh─Б’ or the words ‘svadh─Б namah’, as to wearing the sacred thread in the yaj├▒opavita or pr─Бc─лn─Бvita way and as to the number of ─Бhutis 957

955 a. Terms already explained such as P─Бrvana’ and ‘Ekoddista! are not explained again, Vide n. 855above for those two words. IV 1

Mah─Бpitryaj├▒a in S─Бkamedha

427

formed in S─Бkamedha, the third of the four C─Бturm─Бsyas: “He offers to Soma accompanied by the pitrs a cake baked on six potsherds, to the pitrs Barhisadah (sitting on darbha grass or in a yaj├▒a) fried grains, for the pitrs called Agnisv─Бtta he milks a drink from a cow which has to be won over (to another calf). This for thee, O father and for those who come after thee (i. e. for thy descendants); this for thee, O grandfather, great-grandfather and for those who come after thee; do, yo Pitrs rejoice in your portions. May we gladden thee, O Indra, that castest thy glance at us, come forth now with full chariot seat; being praised (by us) thou goest to places desired by you. Yoke, O Indra, thy two bay steeds. They (pitarah) have eaten, they have rejoiced, the dear ones have dispelled (evil); the radiant sages have been praised with newest hymn, Yoke, O Indra, thy two bay steeds. The pitrs have eaten, the pitrs have rejoiced, the pitrs have been glad, the pitrs have purified themselves. Go away, O Pitrs, that art soma-loving by your majestic ancient paths. Then reach ye the pitrs that well know you (or everything) and that revel in the company of Yama.”

In the Tai.959 Br. I.2.10 the Pindapitryajna is dealt with at some length. In the note below the important passages are set forth leaving out the legends, repetitions and matters not relevant to our purpose: “Therefore the rite (called pinda pitryajia) is performed the day previous (to the Darsesti).

рд╡рд┐ рд░рд╛рд╡рдзрд╛рди Bhandarkar Oriental Research Institute

History of Dharma┼Ы─Бstra

[Vol.

He says ’to Soma drunk by the pitrs, svadh─Бl Adoration!’ He says to Agni, the carrier of kavya, svadh─Б! Adoration ! (Thereby ) he pleases the fire that pertains to the pitrs. He offers (into fire ) three oblations; he puts down (on the darbhas spread on the ground) three pindas. (These) thus come to six in number. Six indeed are the seasons. He (thereby) pleases the seasons. The seasons are indeed the shining (or divine) pitrs……The darbha grass is cut with one stroke; the pitrs have as it were (passed away) once for ever. He puts down thrice (the pindas). The pitrs are indeed in the third world from here. He (thereby) pleases them. He (the performer) turns his face away to the north from the south), for the Fathers are shy. He remains with his face turned away till the steam (of the boiled rice of the pindas) ceases to rise, for the Fathers have the steam of rice as their share; he should simply gmell (the pindas). That as if does not amount to eating or non-eating. The pit┼Щs when departing (from the ┼Ыr─Бddha rite) take away or grant a valiant son. He cuts off the fringe (of a garment to place it on the pindas), for the share of Fathers is taking away (what is offered). He (thereby) allots their proper share to the pitrs (and dismisses them). When the performer) is in the latter part of life (i. e, over 50 years of age) he cuts off hair (from his chest instead of presenting a da┼Ыa). At that time he is nearer to the pitrs (when above 50 years of age). He offers adoration, because adoration (namask─Бra) is dear to the pitrs. Adoration to you, O Fathers, for vigour; adoration to you, O fathers, for life; adoration to you, O fathers, for svadh┼л; adoration to you, O fathers, for ardour; adoration, O fathers, for the terri ble! O fathers! here is adoration to you. This (pindapitryaj├▒a) is indeed a sacrifice of men (i. e. sacrifice to departed men) and other sacrifices belong to the gods.тАЭ In the Tai. Br. I. 4. 10 the Pitryaj├▒a performed in s─Бkamelha is praised (in 2) and further on it is said that Rtus (seasons) are pitrs and they offered pitryaj├▒a to Praj─Бpati, their father. This passage gupports the provision made in Manu and some of the digests that the Rtus are to be identified with pitrs and obeisance is to be made to them. %0

Pindapitryaj├▒a in sat. Br.

429

The Sat. Br. (II. 4. 2) contains the following somewhat fuller account of the Pinda-pitry aj├▒a, omitting legendary or other irrelevant matters :-When the moon is not seen either in the east or in the west, then he (the performer of the Darsa sacrifice) presents food to the Fathers in each month …… He presents it in the afternoon. The forenoon indeed belongs to the gods; the midday to men; and the afternoon to the Fathers; therefore he presents (food to the Fathers) in the afternoon. While seated behind the G─Бrhapatya fire with his face turned towards the south and the sacred thread on his right shoulder he takes that material (for the offering from the cart). There upon he rises from thence and threshes the rice while standing north of the Dak┼Яi┼Жa fire and facing the south. Only once does he clean the rice, for it is once for all that the fathers have passed away. He then boils it. While it stands on the Dak┼Яi┼Жa fire) he pours some clarified butter on it. After remov ing it (from the fire) he offers to the gods two oblations in the fire …… Here he is engaged in a sacrifice to the Fathers; hence he thereby propitiates the gods and being permitted by the gods, he presents that food to the Fathers. He offers to both Agni and Soma … He offers with the formula To Agni, the carrier of kavya (what is offered to the Manes), sv─Бh─Б!’, ‘To Soma accompanied by the Fathers, sv─Бh─Б!’ (V─Бj. S. II 29). He then puts the pot-ladle (mek┼Яana) on the fire, that being in lieu of the Svistak┼Щt. Thereafter he draws (with the sphya, the wooden sword) one line south of the Dak┼Яi┼Жa fire, that being in lieu of the altar. He then lays down a firebrand at the further (south) end of the line, For, were he to present that food to the Fathers without having laid down a firebrand, the Asuras and R─Бk┼Яasas would certainly tamper with it. … He lays it down with the text ‘whatsoever Asuras roam about being attracted by the svadh─Б (offering to Fathers), assuming various shapes, be they large-bodied or small-bodied, may Agni expel them from this world (V─Бj. S. II, 30)… He then takes the water jar and makes the Fathers wash (their hands) merely saying ‘N. N., wash thyself’ (naming) the sacrificer’s father; ‘N. N. wash thy self (naming the sacrificer’s) grandfather; ‘N. N., wash thyself

History of Dharma┼Ы─Бstra

[ Vol.

(naming) the sacrificer’s great-grandfather. As one would pour out water (for a guest) when he is about to take food, so in this case. Now those (stalks of sacrificial grass) are severed with one stroke and cut off near the root; the top belongs to the gods, the middle part to men and the root part (of darbhas) to the fathers. Therefore they are cut off near the roots …… He spreads them along with the line with their tops towards the south. Thereon he presents (to the fathers the three round cakes of rice). He presents thus :- for the gods they offer thus: for men they ladle out; and in the case of the fathers they do in this very way; therefore he presents (the cakes to the fathers) thus. With ‘N. N., this for thee!’ he presents one cake to the sacrificer’s father. Some add ‘for those that come after thee’, but let him not say this, since he himself is one of those to whom it would be offered in common. Let him therefore merely say ‘N, N., this for thee!’ as to the sacrificer’s father; ‘N. N., this for thee’ as to his grandfather; ‘N. N., this for thee’ as to his great grandfather…He then mutters ‘Here, O fathers, regale your selves; like bulls come hither each to his own share!’ (V─Бj. S. II, 31). Whereby he says ‘Eat each his own share’. He then turns round to the left so as to face the opposite (north) side ; for the fathers are far away from men; and thereby he also is far away (from the fathers). ‘Let him remain (standing with bated breath) until his breath fail’ say some; ‘for thus far extends the vital energy’. However, having remained so far a moment-he again turns round (to the right) and mutters ’the Fathers have regaled themselves; like bulls they have come each to his own share’ (V─Бj. S. II, 31); whereby what he says is ’they have eaten each his own share’. Thereupon he takes the water jar and makes them wash themselves (by pouring water on the pipdas), merely saying ‘N. N., wash thyself’ (naming) the sacrificer’s father; ‘N. N. wash thy self’ (naming) his grandfather; ‘N. N., wash thyself’ (naming) his paternal great-grandfather. Even as one would pour out (water for a guest). When he has taken his meal, so it is here. He then pulls down the tuck (of the sacrificer’s garment) and performs obeisance. The tuck is sacred to the Fathers; therefore he performs obeisance to them after pulling down the tuck, … Six times he performs obeisance, for there are six seasons and the fathers are the seasons. He mutters ‘Give us houses, O fathers’ for the fathers are the rulers of houses; and this is the prayer for blessing at this sacrificial performance. After the

monthly ┼Ыr├дddha (m─Бsi-┼Ыr├дddha) is the prakrti of Astak─Б and other sr─Бddhas in which three ancestors are to be invoked. It is as follows: Now then at a P─Бrvana-┼Ыr─Бddha, or at a ┼Ыr─Бddha celebrated for securing some desired object, or at an Abhyu dayika-┼Ыr─Бddha or at an Ekoddista┼Ыr├дddha, the performer causes to sit down br─Бhmaс╣Зas who are endowed with learning, moral character and proper conduct or who are endowed with ( at least) one of these three characteristics ), who have been invited already in proper time, who have taken a bath, whose feet are washed (by the performer) and who have sipped water (taken ─Бcamana), as representatives of (or equal to) the Fathers, with their faces turned to the north, one for each of the Fathers, or two for each or three for each.   1. The rules about Pindapitrya├▒ja have been set forth in ─Аsv. Sr. S. II. 6. N─Бr─Бyana notes (on ─А┼Ыv. gr. IV. 7.2) that ─А┼Ыval─Бyana treats of only the procedure relating to the rite for pitrs and that he does not at all refer to the dinner given to daiva or Vai┼бvadeva br─Бhmanas at the time of sraddha. It is therefore possible that feeding daiva brahmanas was added to the ancient ritual, though it must be said that Manu III. 125, Yaj. I. 224-28 and Vas. XI. 27 prescribe such feeding. Dr. Caland (in ‘Ahnencult p. 161 ) asserts that he can prove that the detail of feeding daiva brahmanas spread from the Sr─Бddhas┼лtra of Katy─Бyana to the other sutras and he relies on the fact that K├дty─Бyana (in Kandik─Б 2) prescribes that the vi┼Ыve dev─Бh should be invoked with the verse . Visve dev─Бsa ─Бgata’ and the performer should mutter the verse visve dev─Бh srnutemam’ which are respectively Vaj. S. VII. 34 and XXXIII. 53. But Dr. Caland tries to prove too much. The first verse occurs twice in the Rg. (II. 41. 13 and VI 52.7) and the second occurs in Rg. VI. 52. 13, Tai. S. II. 4. 14. 5. They are not found only in the Vaj. S. as Dr. Caland seems to have thought. It is possible that other works took over those mantras from the Rgveda or the Tai. S. It may also be noted that Y─Бj. I. 229 mentions only ‘Visve dev─Бsa’ and specifies that it is a rk (and not a mantra or yajus). So Yaj. at least does not appear to have borrowed the prescriptions of Katyayana. It is not necessary to examine the other arguments.

From considerations of space it is impossible to set out all the differences among the several grhyas┼лtras of the Rgveda, of the Taittiriya s─Бkh─Б (viz. Baudh─Бyana, ─Аp., Hir., Bharadv─Бja and Vaikh─Бnasa), of the V─Бjasaneya s─Бkh─Б (such as Sr─Бddhas┼лtra of K─Бty─Бyana), of the S─Бmaveda (such as Gobhila and Kh─Бdira) and of the Atharvaveda (being Kausika s┼лtra). A few matters may be set out by way of illustration. The ─Аp. gr. (21. 3-4)981 states that after the br─Бhmaс╣Зas are invited for ┼Ыr─Бddha dinner) from the food prepared for the dinner a portion is taken out in a vessel and therefrom seven ─Бhutis are cast into the fire with the seven mantras beginning with ‘yan me m─Бt─Б’ (in ─Аp. M. P. II. 19, 1-7), the first two for the father, the next two for the grand-father, next two for the great-grand-father and the 7th to pitrs in general with sv─Бh─Б (but without naming any one) and then six oblations of clarified butter are offered with the six formulas beginning with ‘sv─Бh─Б pitre’ (Ap. M. P. II. 19, 8-13). Thus the agnaukarana in Ap. consists of two parts viz, ─Бhutis of food and of clarified butter, while in Asv. it is made only with food. Then the performer should touch all food (cooked food and the remainder of what is employed for offering into fire ) with the three mantras “esa te tata madhum─Бn’ (Ap. M. P. II. 19. 14-16), he should make the br─Бhmaс╣Зas touch the food served to each with the Yajus formula ’the earth is thy vessel’ (Ap. M. P. 2. 20. 1) quoted in n. 992 below.

Ap. gr. prescribes the mantra, ‘putr─Бn pautr─Бn’ (Ap. M. P. II. 20. 24) for moistening the pindas, while Baud. gr. and Vaikh─Бnasa gr. (IV. 6) employ the mantra “├╝rjam vahantir’ (V─Бj. S. II, 34) for the same purpose. It may be noted that

980 a. It will be noticed that ─Аsv. omits several details viz. (1) he does not say that the br─Бhmaс╣Зas for all the gods are to be seated, facing the east; (2) he mentions no mantra such as ‘ye agnidadgh├г &c.;’ (3) nothing is said about dak┼Яin─Б or about the performer following the brahmanas a few paces and then returning with their permission.

these s┼лtras which belong to the Taittiriya sakh─Б employ a Verse from another recension viz. the Sukla Yajurveda.

The Hir. Gr. (II. 10-13) is more elaborate than the Ap. Gr. and not only sets out at length many of the mantras in ─Аp. M. P. II. 19-20, but adds some more. The Sr─Бddhas┼лtra of K─Бty─Бyana (1-3) sets out the procedure of the monthly sraddha almost in the same way as the Y─Бj├▒avalkyasmrti (which is set out below). It states that in the monthly ┼Ыr─Бddha first come the daiva rites and then the various items occur as in the Pinda-pitryaj├▒a pindapitryaj├▒a-vad-upac─Бraс╕е’ (first s┼лtra of the 2nd kandik─Б). Some details which it contains (and Y─Бj. does not expressly mention) may be set out here. It gives in full the mantras “tilosi’, ‘y─Б divya’ (both of which occur in A┼бv. gr.), ‘prthivi to p─Бtram’ (which is ─Аp. M. P. II, 20.1). It prescribes that in addition to the G─Бyatri and the Madhumati verses the word ‘madhu’ should be repeated thrice. The holy texts to be repeated while the br─Бhmaс╣Зas are engaged in eating according to K─Бty─Бyana are the G─Бyatri (once or thrice), the five R─Бk┼Яoghni verses (Rg. IV. 4.1-5, Vaj. S. XIII. 9-13, Tai. S. T. 2. 14. 1-2). Purusas┼лkta, the Apratiratha hymn (Rg X. 103. 1-13 = Vaj. S. 17. 33-34, 46 = Tai. S. IV. 6. 4. 1-4) and others. It expressly states that the svadh─Бv─Бcana (Y─Бj. I. 244) relates to both paternal and maternal ancestors. Besides the blessing contained in Y─Бj. I. 246, Katy─Бyana provides that the performer is to pray for and the br─Бhmaс╣Зas are to pronounce two more viz. May the pitrs be kind (lit. not dreadful) to us’ and ‘May our family prosper’. Dr. Caland in his learned work ‘Altindi scher Ahnencult’ (pp. 150тАУ152) appears inclined to hold that when a s┼лtrak─Бra has not actually said anything on certain items in the ┼Ыr─Бddha ritual, one has no right to anticipate, on the authority of later authors, that those items existed in the times of that s┼лtrak─Бra. I demur to this conclusion. Dr. Caland has attached no weight to the fact that Jaimini (as stated in H. of Dh, vol. III p. 870) laid down the principle that one may include certain items from another s─Бkh─Б. Jaimini’s s┼лtras cannot be supposed to have laid down those propositions for the first time. Jaimini’s s┼лtras are at least as old as some of the extant srauta s├╝tras such as that of Katy─Бyana. Therefore hardly any chrono logical conclusions can be drawn with certainty from the silence of a s┼лtrak─Бra as to a certain item in the ┼Ыr─Бddha ritual.

The story is very clearly set out in errat 1, Chapters 21-24 and the Matsyapurana chap. 20-21. Sever pupils of Garga guarding their guru’s cow thought of eating that cow as they were famished. But the youngest said ’let us make use of the cow’s flesh in sraddha, so that we may be saved from sin’. Two of the brothers became daiva brahmanas, three became pitr-br─Бhmanas, one became the giver and the 7th became a guest, They told the guru that the cow was eaten by a tiger. They passed through several births first as seven hunters, then deer in Kala├▒jara bill and so on. Sraddha ultimately saved them. The same story is narrated in Padma V. 10.49-125, and v. 47.282-304 (in which last the disciples are said to have been those of any). After becoming hamsas three of them became kings (a king and two ministers, acc. to FET) and cared not for the other world. The four others knew the path to moksa, sent word to the three with these verses saying that they four had started on the long road to the other world (Frat…arci) and asking the other three not to be immersed in the mire of wordliness (77… ). The story also occurs in the BERTIOT (SATIEAT chap. 41.24 ff). It is interesting to note that in the Jaina Uttaradhyayana-s┼лtra (S. B. It should be noticed how closely the Padmapurana follows the procedure (including the mantras ) contained in Y─Бj├▒a valkya. What procedure the author of a Pur─Б┼Жa follows depends upon his learning and the s┼лtra that he studied. For example, the Visnudharmottara 1.140 appears to rely on the Ap.gr. and the Ap. M. P. (II. 19-20), since I. 140, 12 refers to ─Аp. M. P. II, 19.1., 1. 140.29-30 to Ap. M. P. II. 19. 14-16, I. 140. 35 to ─Аp. M. P. II, 20.1. Similarly, Skanda (VI. 224. 3-51) closely follows ─А┼Ыv. gr and Y─Бj.

IV] The maxim of ‘sarvasakh─Бpratyaya’ 453 the several items found in other s├╝tras and smrtis though not included in the kalpa or grhya s┼лtra of his own S─Бkh─Б. This topic is discussed at great length by Hem─Бdri (on sr─Бddha ) pp. 748-759 and briefly by Medh─Бtithi on Manu II, 29 and XI.216, by the Mit, on Y─Бj. III. 325, Apar─Бrka p. 1053 and others. Those who are for strictly following the details in one’s own s┼лtra alone argue as follows: If one were at liberty to include details other than those contained in one’s own s┼лtra, the order of the details ( krama) given in one’s sutra and the time specified for each detail would be interfered with. Besides, if the addition of details were permissible, one would be liable to the charge of giving up the usages of one’s own family handed down for generations. These objectors rely upon such passages as that of the Visnudharmottara which states ‘He who violating (the dictates of ) his own s┼лtra acts according to a sutra meant for others, treats thereby his own sage ( the author of his s┼лtra ) as unauthoritative and incurs (the blame of) doing what is im proper.’ 1010 The smrtis that contain additional details may be meant for those men who have no kalpa or grhya s├╝tra of their own or they may be useful for ┼Ъ┼лdras.

Those who espouse the view that as far as possible all details found in several grhyas┼лtras and smrtis on one rite should be included by every one rely mainly on Jaimini II. 4. 8-33 which is called ‘sakh─Бntar─Бdhikaranany─Бya’ or ‘sarvas─Бkh─Бpratyaya ny─Бya’. The principal sutra is Jai. II. 4. 9.1011 It is established in this g┼лtra that the prayoiana (purpose ) or phala (reward to be secured) of the rite is the same in different s┼лtras and smrtis. For example, the rewards of ┼Ыr─Бddha are stated to be the same in all s┼лtras and smс╗Щtis (vide notes 787-790 above); then the dravya (materials) and the deity are the same (in Parvana ┼Ыr─Бddha the deities are the paternal ancestors and the materials,

viz. ku┼Ыas, tilas, water, vessels, foods &c. are the same in all works). The effort that is enjoined the vidhi) is the same and the name (P─Бrvana┼Ыr─Бddha, Ekoddista sraddha &c.) is the same. Therefore, on account of these various signs one easily recog nizes that the same rite is being dealt with by all s┼лtras, even if many of them differ in details. It cannot be said that smrtis will be useful for those who have no sutras of their own. Each man of the first three var┼Жas is attached to some s┼лtra or other by the tradition of his family or caste. Similarly, the smrtis cannot be held to be meant for s┼лdras alone, since the smrtis mainly deal with upanayana, the study of the Vedas, agnihotra and other matters with which a s┼лdra has no concern. Similar ly, the objection that if details were allowed to be inserted from other s┼лtras and smrtis the krama and k─Бla prescribed in one’s S┼лtra might have to be set aside, the reply is contained in Jai. I. 3. 5-7 (explained at great length in H. of Dh. vol. III. pp. 841-848 ).1012 The fruti says after getting ready a bundle of kusa grass he prepares the vedi (altar)’. Here a certain order of acts is laid down. If after a bundle of ku┼бas is got ready, the man has a sneeze, he has to sip water (perform ┼лcamana ) immediately as laid down by Manu V. 145 and Vas. III. 38 before he prepares the vedi. So the objector says the krama will be interfered with. The reply is that the sequence (krama) is only a characteristic of the items in the ┼Ыruti passage, that all that is meant is that the making of the altar follows the getting ready of a kusa bundle, but that it is not meant that the making of the vedi should follow immediately after the bundle is got ready. Therefore, the conclusion is that whatever detail is not in conflict with one’s own s─Бkh─Б or sutra may be in cluded in the rite one is about to perform, but if there is a direct conflict, then one should stick to one’s own s┼лtra. As observed by K├дty─Бyana ‘whatever is declared, whether in great detail or in brief, in one’s own grhyas┼лtra about a rite, if he performs that much, it may be taken that he has done all that is required of him; but what is not handed down in one’s s─Бkh─Б (or s┼лtra) but is contained in another s─Бkh─Б and is not in conflict with one’s ovn s─Бkh─Б, should be performed by the learned, as in the case of

Maxim of

sarvas─Бkh─Бpratyaya’

agnihotra and the like’. 1013 The first verse of Katyayana may be explained as applying where one’s s─Бkh─Б or s┼лtra deals with a matter without requiring any addition or as the next best course where one is not able to supplement one’s s┼лtra owing to some unseen cause or owing to human difficulties. The Sangraha says that where different items of the ┼Ыr─Бddha rite are declared to be performed at different times and there is no agreement among the sages, one should follow one’s grhya sutra, but where one’s grhyas┼лtra is silent as to a certain item or as to the stage when it is to be performed, there is an option and one may follow the opinion of some gage as to that item. 1014 It appears that even the ancient grhya s┼лtras exhibit tendencies that led to the sarvas─Бkh─Б-pratyaya-ny─Бya e. g. A┼бv. gr. (q. in n. 966) employs several passages (such as ‘Tilosi’, ‘Ya. divy─Б,’ which do not occur in the Rgveda.)

It is owing to this maxim of ‘sarvas─Бkh─Б-pratyayany─Бya’ that medieval digests go on heaping up details from all smrtis and pur─Бс╣Зas in their descriptions of the several ┼бr─Бddhas, the procedures of which were not originally very extensive.

History of Dharma┼Ы─Бstra

I Vol.

An important question which exercised the minds of many medieval writers was ‘who was the real recipient (samprad─Бna)1023 of the offerings made in ┼Ыr─Бddha, whether the br─Бhmaс╣Зas or the pitrs’. Relying on the words of the ─А┼Ыv. gr. IV.8.1 (quoted above in n. 966 etasmin k─Бle … d─Бnam) and passages of the pur─Б┼Жas such as the Var─Бha (13. 51) ‘vibhave sati viprebhyo asm─Бn uddi┼Ыya d─Бsyati’, the Mah─Бrnavaprak─Б┼Ыa, Harihara and some others held that br─Бhmaс╣Зas were the recipients, while others like Sridatta, relying on indications furnished by ┼Ыruti passages like V─Бj. S. 19. 36 (ak┼Яan pitarah amimadanta pitarah) and such formulas as ‘pitar-etat te arghyam’ or ’etadvah pitaro v─Бsaс╕е,’ held that the real recipients intended were the pitrs, but, as the pitrs had gone to another world and could not be bodily present to receive the gifts of such things as sandlewood paste, flowers and clothes, the latter were only handed over or assigned to the br─Бhmaс╣Зas who were for the moment contemplated as not different from the pitrs.1023a Vide Sm. C. (┼Ыr─Бddha pp. 447 449 ), ┼Ъr. Pr. pp. 30-31 for a discussion of these two view points. It should, however, be noted that the water given to the br─Бhmaс╣Зas and the dak┼Яi┼Ж─Б given to them were only meant for the br─Бhmanas, the former for purification and the latter for the inexhaustible merit that dak┼Яi┼Ж─Б to br─Бhmanas conferred.

It is to be noted that in the invocation (─Бv─Бhana) of the pitrs there is a divergence of views as to the mantras to be employed and also as to the stage when it is to be made. Hem─Бdri (┼Ыr─Бddha, pp. 1254-56) states that there were five different views on the latter point, the three most important of which were that ─Бv─Бhana should come before giving darbhas as ─Бsana on the left side of the seats of the pitrya br─Бhmanas or after giving such darbhas or after agnaukara├▒a. As regards the former (viz. the mantras), Y─Бj. (I. 232-233), the Brahm─Бnda pur─Бna and several others say that the invocation mantra is * u┼Ыantas-tv─Б’ (Rg. X. 16. 12, V─Бj. S. 19. 70, Tai. S. II. 6.12.1) and after the ─Бv─Бhana the performer should perform japa of the verse ‘a yantu nah’ (V─Бj. S. 19.58). The Vi┼Яnudharma sutra1024 (73. 10-12) states the performer after having received

Another important question on which there is great diver gence concerns the number of ─Бhutis to be offered in agnau karana, the deities to whom the homa was to be offered, the order in which the deities were to be named and the form of words to be used. On these matters there appears to have been divergent views from very ancient times. According to the ┼Ъat. Br. II, 4. 2. 12-13 the ─Бhutis were only 1027 two, they were offered to Agni and Soma in that order and the word sv─Бh─Б was used at the end. According to the Tai. Br. I, 3.10.2тАУ3 1028 the ─Бhutis were three, they were to be offered to Soma, Agni and to Yama in that order and the formula ended with ‘svadh─Б namah’ (and not with ‘sv─Бh─Б’). It is therefore that a verse of K─Бty─Б yana 1029 says " whether to employ the word ‘sv─Бh─Б’ or the words

svadh─Б namah’, whether and when to wear the sacred chord in the yaj├▒opav─лta form or pr├дcin─Бvita form and what was to be the number of ─Бhutis-all these have to be understood from one’s own s┼лtra.” The difference of views which is noticed as far back as the Br─Бhmanas persists in the s├╝tras, smrtis, pur─Бnas and is briefly indicated here. IV]

Rules about serving food

465

side dishes viz. broths, vegetables, milk, curds, gheo and honey on the ground and not on a wooden stool or the like). The vessels placed on the ground should contain various kinds of food (such as sweetmeats, p─Бyasa ), fruits and roots, delicious flesh, spiced or perfumed drinks. Having brought near the br─Бhmanas all the vessels containing food, he should serve it in the plates declaring the characteristic of each kind of food (saying this is sweet, this is sour’ &c.). The performer while serving should not shed tears (remembering his ancestors ), he should not become angry, should not utter falsehood, he should not touch the vessel containing ) food with his foot and should not serve food with a violent jerk. Whatever is liked by the brahmanas should be served to them without any grumbling and he should talk about Brahma (or about Vedic riddles ), because that is agreeable to the pitrs. The performer himself, being pleased, should ( by his sweet speech ) gladden the br─Бhmaс╣Зas, should make them partake of food without hurry, and should urge them on frequently (to take more food) by declaring the good points of the various items of food. All food should be steaming hot and the br─Бhmaс╣Зas should partake of it silently and should not themselves speak of the good points of the food even when questioned by the performer. When the food is hot, when the br─Бhmaс╣Зas eat in silence and when the good qualities of the food are not declared by the br─Бhmapas, the Fathers partake of it. When a br─Бhmana (at a ┼Ыr─Бddha dinner) partakes of food, having his head covered with a garment (a turban &c )or facing the south or having his sandals on, evil spirits partake of the food (and not the Fathers).’ As early as Gaut., it is provided that the food for the br─Бhmanas should be of the highest sort and should be enriched by condiments and flavoured.

Some of the other rules are : The Praj─Бpati-smrti (verses 57-62 ) states who should cook the food for the ┼Ыr─Бddha dinner. The wife, any fortunate (or handsome) woman of the performer’s gotra whose husband is living and who has a son or brother and is devoted to waiting upon her elders, the performer’s teacher’s wife, his maternal uncle’s wife, paternal or maternal aunt, his sister, his daughter or daughter-in-law, all of them having their husbands alive, should engage in the cooking, of the food for ┼Ыr─Бddha. Women of good family, who hayo a large progeny, whose husbands are alive and who are about 50.yoats old or these women if they have become widows, and the wife of one’s paternal uncle or brother, one’s mothers (natupator

step-mothers ) and the mothers of one’s father may cook the ┼Ыr─Бddha food and also a woman of the same gotra who is mild by temper. In the Anu┼б─Бsana parva (92.15) it is stated that a woman belonging to a gotra other than that of the deceased should not be employed for cooking ┼Ыr├дddha food. One’s brother, paternal uncle, brother’s son, sister’s son, one’s son, pupil, one’s daughter’s son or daughter’s husband may also engage in cook ing the ┼Ыr─Бddha food, but not a woman who wears a white and wet garment, who has let her hair loose, who does not wear a bodice, who is ill or who has bathed her head. Before the br─Бhmanas begin to eat, the food should be first served in the plates for the Vai┼Ыvadeva br─Бhmaс╣Зas and then in those of the pitrya br─Бhmaс╣Зas (Vi┼Яnu Dh. S. 173. 13-14), but once the br─Бhmaс╣Зas have begun to eat there is no such precedence; what ever each br─Бhmaс╣Зa may be noted as requiring should be served to him (as indicated by Manu III, 231). The performer of the ┼Ыr├дddha when serving food to the br─Бhmanas (including pitrya) wears his sacred thread in the upavita form. Though it is said that the food should be hot, that does not apply to such eatables as curds, fruits and roots and flavoured 1035 drinks (as Sankha XIV.13 and Skandapur─Бna say ). As Hem─Бdri (┼Ыr─Бddha p. 1371) points out, the serving of food in a ┼Ыr─Бddha rite should be done with the right hand supported by the left; besides, nothing should be served with the bare hand or with a single hand, but with a wooden ladle or other utensil (but not an iron one). All cooked food, all side dishes and ghee should be served with a ladle (and not with the bare hand) but not water or eatables like laddus. No salt was to be directly served (Vispu Dh. S, 79.12). except by signs made with the hand.’ Whatever is offered in a brahmana’s hand (by way of agnaukarana) and whatever food is placed in the plates should be mixed up and eaten Hem─Бdri quotes passages from the Maitr─Бyaniya-s┼лtra and from the Skandapur─Б┼Жa setting out the mantras wherewith certain articles were to be served; e. g. the Skandapur─Бna says that p─Бyasa should be served with the verse ’namo vah pitaro’ (V─Бj. S. II. 32. Tai. S. III, 2.5.5), clarified butter with the mantra Tejosi sukram’, curds with the mantra “dadhikr─Бvno’ (Rg. IV. 39.6, V─Бj. S. 23. 32, Tai. S. 1. 5. 11. 4). Ap. Dh, S. (II. 8. 18. 11) provides that the leavings of a ┼Ыr─Бddha dinner should not be given to one who is inferior to the invited br─Бhmanas in qualities and Manu III, 249 states that the man who after eating ┼Ыr─Бddha dinner gives the leavings to a ┼Ы├╝dra falls in the K─Бlas┼лtra Hell.

The Matsyapur─Бna and some other works provide that the br─Бhmaс╣Зas should pronounce blessings on the performer (who faces the east) after they have sipped water and have been given water, flowers and ak┼Яata grains. The performer prays ‘May our Fathers be not terrible (i, e, be kind) to us. The br─Бhmanas reply “let it be so’. The performer prays ‘May our family grow’, ‘May donors increase in our family and also food’, тАШMay these blessings turn out to be true’. To all these the br─Бhmanas reply after each one of the prayers 1040 “May it be so’. There are rules about the time when the leavings or particles of food in the plates of the br─Бhmanas that ate the dinner should be removed or swept away. Vas. (XI. 21-22) and the K┼лrma pur─Б┼Жa provide that the leavings of food should not be removed till the Sun sets, since streams of nectar flow from them, which are drunk by the spirits of) those departed persons for whom no water was offered. Manu III. 265 (which is the same as Matsya 17.56 and Padma, Srstikhanda 9.185) provides another rule that the leavings of the food in the plates may remain where they are till the br─Бhmapas are dismissed and depart.

Rules about removal of leavings

469

Hemadri (Sraddha, p. 1512 )1041 therefore provides that if the per former has another house the leavings may not be removed till sunset, but if he has only one house, they may be removed after the br─Бhmanas have gone away (vide Y─Бj. I. 257, Matsya 17.56 ). It is further provided by Brhaspati 1042 that the plates should not be removed before the br─Бhmanas pronounce the word ‘svasti’, and Jat─Бkarnya 1043 and the Skandapurana say that the plates and the leavings should be removed by the performer himself or by his pupil or son, but not by women nor by a child nor by one who is not of the same caste. Manu III. 258 provides that, after the br─Бhmanas have left, the performer should look at the south and pray to the pitrs for certain blessings contained in Manu III, 259 which are the same as Y─Бj. I 246 translated above (vide p. 447), Visnu Dh. S. 73.28, Matsya 16.49-50. The Ap. gr. 20.9 (q. in note 981), Ap. Dh. S. II. 7. 17.16, Manu III, 264, Y─Бj. I. 249 provide that the performer should partake of the remainder of the food cooked for the ┼Ыr─Бddha along with his wife, paternal and maternal relatives after recit ing (according to Haradatta) the Y─Бjusa mantra (Ap. M. P. II. 20.26) which means ’entering the life breath I offer nectar; my soul is centred in Brahman for the sake of immortality. The Ap. gr. and Ap. Dh. S. provide 1044 that the performer must eat at least a morsel of the food left after serving to the br├дhmanas. Vy─Бsa and Devala prescribe that on the day of ┼Ыr├дddha the per former must not observe a fast (even if he usually does so as on Ek─Бda┼Ы─л or Sivar─Бtra). A way out was provided by the Bra hmavaivarta-purana by recommending that the performer should merely smell the remnants of the ┼Ыr├дddha food. Vide

Hem─Бdri (┼Ыr─Бddha, pp. 1519-1521) for the discussion. Hem─Бdri (p. 1485) refers to the practice (observed even now) that after the performer receives the blessings referred to above, his son, grandson and the like should offer adoration to the devat─Бs in the form of pindas. There were several views as to the exact stage at which the offerings of pindas were to be made. According to S─Бn. Gr. IV. 1.9., ─А┼Ыv. gr. IV. 8. 12, 1047 Sankha 14.11, Manu III. 260-261, Y─Бj. The pindas are made with boiled rice mixed with sesame and are placed on darbhas on a clean spot and at a distance of about one aratni from 1048 the plates in which the br─Бhmanas ate and the performer faces the south. Here again there are two opinions, one being that pindas were to be offered before the br─Бhmaс╣Зas sip water (perform ─Бcamana) after dinner (e. g. ├Д┼Ыv. gr. pi┼Жdad─Бna in Samvatsarika sr─Бddha, Mah─Бlaya and the like (p. 164).

There is another conflict of views as regards the ancestors to whom pindas are to be offered at the ┼Ыr─Бddha on am─Бv─Бsya. Most of the ancient Vedic works refer only to the three paternal ancestors as the devat─Бs of the P─Бrvana-┼Ыr─Бddha and not to any other relatives. The three paternal ancestors are separately the devat─Бs of ┼Ыr─Бddha and not cumulatively, as indicated by the ─А┼Ыv. Srauta II. 6.15 and Vi┼Яnu Dh. S. 73.13-14. The important questions are whether the wives of the paternal ancestors, viz, the mother, the grandmother and the paternal great-grandmother were associated with their husbands in ancient times and secondly, whether the three paternal ancestors of one’s mother viz. the maternal grandfather, the maternal great-grandfather and the maternal great-great-grandfather were invoked together with their wives in the P─Бrvana. The answer to both these questions so far as the Vedas and Br─Бhmanas are concerned is in the negative, Vide Tai. S. I. 8. 5.1, Tai. Br. I. 3. 10, II, 6. 16, V─Бj. S. 19. 36-37, Sat. Br. II, 4.2. 16, in all of which the only persons expressly named are the pitrs and three paternal ancestors. It may be noted, however, that in V─Бj. S. 9. 19 (which is cited by K─Бty─Бyana at the end of Sr─Бddhas┼лtra 3 as the mantra to be recited when following the br─Бhmaс╣Зas that are dismissed) there is a clear reference to paternal ancestors and also to mothers. Almost all s┼лtras also are silent as regards the invocation of the maternal ancestors in P─Бrva┼Жa-┼Ыr─Бddha along with paternal ones. Vide 1053 ─А┼Ыv. ┼Ъr.; Sudargana on Ap. gr. VIII. 21. 2 states that the S┼лtrak─Бra and Bh─Бsyak─Бra did not speak of M─Бt─Бmaha┼Ыr─Бddha as it is not obligatory for a daughter’s son to offer it. IV1 Ancestors to whom pindas were offered 473 ancestors. The Gobhilasmrti provides 1055 that six pindas should be offered except in the Anvastak─Б┼Ыr─Бddha, the first ┼Ыr├дddha (on the 11th day), the sixteen ┼Ыr─Бddhas and the yearly ┼Ыr─Бddha for a deceased person. Dhaumya 1056 prescribes that where the paternal ancestors are honoured (or fed) the mater nal ancestors also should be certainly honoured without making any difference (between the two classes ); if he makes a dis tinction the performer will go to Hell. The Vi┼Яnupur─Бna, 1057 the Brahm─Бndapurana and the Var─Бhapur─Бna say that some hold that a ┼Ыr─Бddha for maternal ancestors is to be performed separately while other sages hold that one ┼Ыr─Бddha is to be offered at the same time to the paternal and maternal ancestors. Bphaspati (q. by Kalpataru on ┼Ыr─Бddha p. 204) prescribes 1058 that one should offer pindas made from all food cooked for the ┼Ыr─Бddha and mixed with honey and sesamum grains for both paternal and maternal ancestors according to the rules of one’s grhyas┼лtra. The Var─Бhapur─Бna (14. 40-41) says that pitrya brahmanas should be dismissed first and then the daiva br─Бh manas together with those for the mother’s ancestors and that separate pindas were to be offered to the mother’s paternal ancestors (14.37). Some held the view that the offering of pindas to maternal ancestors was obligatory for the putrik─Б putra 1059 (son of the appointed daughter) or for a daughter’s son that inherited the wealth of his maternal grandfather. Brhat-Par─Б┼Ыara (chap. V. p. 153) montions several views on this point. It seems probable that when the appointment of a

History of Dharma┼Ы─Бstra

daughter as a son became rare or went out of vogue the maternal ancestors came to be associated with the paternal ancestors in p─Бrvana-┼Ыr─Бddha.

The question when the wives of ancestors became associa ted with the male ancestors cannot be solved satisfactorily. The pit─Бmahi is not mentioned in the extant. Vedic Literature. But it is certain that the wives of male ancestors had come to be associated with their husbands in the sutra period. For example, the Hir. Gr. II, 10 associates the mother, the paternal grandmother and the paternal great-grandmother with their respective husbands in the monthly ┼Ыr─Бddha performed in the dark half. Similarly, the Baud. gr. II. 11.34 not only associates in the Astak─Б ┼Ыr├дddha the male maternal ancestors with the male paternal ancestors, but also their respective wives. The ─Аp, M. P. 1060 has mantras referring to the three male paternal ancestors as well as their wives. The S─Бn. gr. (IV. 1.11) pro vides that behind the lumps for the paternal ancestors the per former places the lumps for their wives, putting something between the two sets of pindas and the commentator explains that darbhas are placed between the two sets. The Kausika s┼лtra (88.12) also provides for the offering of pi┼Жdas to the wives of male ancestors to the south of the pindas for male ancestors. The ─А┼Ыv. gr. (II. 5. 4-5), while speaking of the Anvas takya rite, refers to pindas to be offered to the wives of ances tors with the addition of rum and the scum of boiled rice. The Vaikh─Бnasa-sm─Бrta-s┼лtra IV. 7 (after describing the Pinda pitryaj├▒a in IV.5-6) notes that the difference between it and the ordinary monthly sraddha is that in the latter pindas are offered to the wives of the pitrs 1061. Dr. Caland (in ‘Ahnencult’ p. 164) thinks that this inclusion of the women ancestors among those to whom pindas were to be offered was made by taking over from Anvastakya ceremonial described above. This con jecture does not look very probable. The Astak─Б rites existed from remote antiquity as shown above. If the offering of pindas to women ancestors were borrowed from the Anvastakya

IV)

Participation of females in pindas offered

475

this item would have figured in all s┼лtras just as Astak─Б ┼Ыra ddha does. It is rather more probable that the extension to women was a natural growth in course of time. Some of the smrtis emphasize the participation of the wives of paternal ancestors in the p─Бrvanasroddha offerings. Satatapa states 1062 : “In what is offered to the pitrs after Sapi┼Жdikarana, the mother is a participant everywhere. A ┼Ыr├дddha may be separately offered to the mother in the Anva┼Яtak─Б rites, in Vrddhi-┼Ыr─Бddha, at Gay─Б and on the anniversary of the day of her death; but in other cases it is performed along with the husband’. It is stated by Brhaspati that the mother partakes of the ┼Ыr─Бddha food along with her husband (i. e. the father of the performer); that the same rule applies to the paternal grandmother and the paternal great-grandmother 1063. The Kalpataru 1064 and others held that the wives of the paternal ancestors were not devat─Бs in the p─Бrva┼Жa-┼Ыr─Бddha, but they only enjoyed the ethereal food which came to the pit┼Щs, while Hem─Бdri and other sou thern writers held that the mother and other female ancestors were among the devat─Бs of p─Бrva┼Жa-┼Ыr├дddha, but not the step mother. As regards the mantra to be recited when offering each of the pindas there is some divergence of views, which reaches far into antiquity. The pinda 1066 is offered to each ancestor after stating his gotra, his relationship to the performer and name (all in the vocative). According to several writers the form of the presentation of the pinda is ’this is for thee, O Father! N.

N. (by name) and so and so by gotra.’ In the Tai. S. I. 8.5 1, in the Ap. M. P. II. 20.13 and in some sutras, the following is added

and for those who follow thee’ (ye ca tv─Бm-anu). 1067 In the Gobhila-grhya IV. 3.6 and Kh─Бdiragrhya the formula is still longer ‘This pinda is thine, O fatherland of those who follow thee and of those whom thou followest. 1068 To thee, Svadha!’. Mantras at offering pindas

477

  • the usage of the Tai.s. in this matter, the reason being 10ro that when the son offers a pinda to his father and employs the formula ’this is thine and of those that follow thee, he would be included among those that follow the father and be thus offering a pinda to himself, which is inauspicious. It is provided by Gobhila-grhya 1071 that if he does not know the names of his ancestors he should put down the first pinda with the Formula

svadh─Б to the Fathers dwelling on the earth’, (he should put down) the 2nd pinda with the formula ‘svadh─Б to the fathers dwelling in the air’, the third with the formula тАШsvadha to the Fathers dwelling in heaven’ and should recite in a low voice the words ‘Here, O Fathers, gladden yourselves, show your vigour each according to his own part.’ Yama quoted by Kalpataru (on Sr. p. 203), following Gobhila provides generally (whether the ancestors be known or not) that the first pinda should be offered to the father with the expression prthivi’, the second to the grandfather in the aerial regions and the third to the paternal great-grandfather with the mantra ‘dyaur darvi’. The Visnu Dh.S. (73.17-19) has similar provisions, the mantras respectively being prthivi darviraksita’, ‘antariksam darvi raksita,’ dyaur-darviraksita’. Medhatithi on Manu III. 194 says (following ASv. Sr. and others) that if the names of the ancestors are not known he should simply say тАЬO Father, Grandfather’ &c. If the gotra be not known then he should employ the gotra name Ka┼Ыyapa. 1072

1 Vol. size of the pi┼Жdas. Marici (quoted by Apar─Бrka p. 507) provides that in p─Бrva┼Жa-┼Ыr─Бddha the pi┼Жda should be of the size of

undried ─Бmalaka fruit, of the size of a bilva fruit in Ekoddista, - in nava┼Ыr─Бddhas the pinda should be bigger than in any one of

the preceding when offered every day during the days of impu rity on death. The Skandapur─Б┼Жa says that pindas should be of such a size as would enable a calf two years old to put it easily into its mouth. 1073 Angiras (q. by Sm. C. p. 475 and Hem─Бdri, ┼Ыr─Бddha p. 1429) prescribes that the pindas may be of the size of kapittha or bilva fruit or of the size of a hen’s egg or of an ─Бmalaka or badara fruit. In the Maitr─Бyaс╣З─лya-s┼лtra 1094 it is said that the pinda for the paternal grandfather should be bigger than that for the father and should be in the middle (of the three pindas), that the pinda for the great-grandfather should be the largest of all. The next point is from what materials the pindas were to be made. If pindas were offered before agnau karana they were to be made from the boiled rice (caru) prepared for agnaukarana. If made after agnaukarana, the pindas were to be made from the cooked food (remaining after agnaukarana) mixed with sesamum (vide Y─Бj. I. 242). If pindas were to be offered after the br─Бhmanas took their dinner, the pindas were to be made from the remainder of the food cooked for the br─Бhmaс╣Зas which was to be mixed with the boiled rice for agnaukara├▒a as stated in K─Бty─Бyana’s Sr─Бddha s┼лtra 1075 The pindas were to be placed according to the Matsya 1076 on darbhas spread on the ground cleaned with water mixed with cow’s dung and urine. There were others such as Devala, the Brahmapur─Б┼Жa and Bhavisyapur─Бna that prescribed that an altar, either circular or square, of sand was to be raised on ground 4 fingers in height and one cubit in extent near the plates from which br─Бhmaс╣Зas were to eat and thereon darbhas

480

About the final disposal (pratipatti) of the pipdas several views were entertained. We have already seen (note 780 ) that the V─Бj. S. and several s┼лtras provided that the middle one of the three pindas for paternal ancestors was to be eaten by the wife of the performer of the ┼Ыr─Бddha if she was desirous of a son. Manu (III. 262-263) provides that the dharmapatni (i. e, a wife of the same varpa and married before any other wife ) should eat the middle pinda with the mantra ‘─Бdhatta pitaro garbham’ (q. in n. 780) and then she gives birth to a son who lives long, secures fame, is intelligent and obtains wealth and progeny and who is of a good and righteous turn of mind. The same rule is provided for by the Laghu-A┼бval─Бyana 23.83, the K┼лrma II. 2. 71, 76, Matsya 16,52, V─Бyu 76,31, Vi┼Яnudharmottara I. 1718, 220, 149, Padma (srstikhanda 9.121) and other pur─Б┼Жas. As regards pindas in general, the ─А┼Ыv. Sr. (11. 7. 14-17) says that the other two pindas (except the middle one ) should be cast into water or in fire or they may be eaten by a br─Бhmana who has suddenly developed a distaste for food or they may be partaken by one who has been suffering from a serious disease (such as tuberculosis or leprosy ) and that in the latter case the man either recovers or dies. The Gobhila-gr. (IV. 3, 31-34) provides that the pindas should be thrown into water or in fire or should be given to a br─Бhmaс╣Зa or a cow to eat. Manu (III. 260-261 ) says the same and adds that they may be given to a goat for eating and that some allow them to be devoured by birds. Y─Бj. I. 257, Matsya 16.52-53, and Padma1079 mention the same five ways of disposal but the last adds one more viz. placing them near a mound of earth. The Varaha pur─Б┼Жa 1080 (190.121 ) says that the performer may eat the first pinda himself, he should give the middle to his wife and the third he should cast into water. The Anu┼б─Бsanaparva (125.25.26) provides that the first and the third should be thrown into water or fire and the middle pinda should be eaten by the wife. It is provided by Bс╗Лhaspati that if the wife is suffering from a disease or is already pregnant or is staying in some other

The Vi┼Яnudharmottara (I. 141, 8) prescribes that when a ┼Ыr─Бddha is performed at a tirtha, the pindas should be cast into the sacred water. The Anu┼б─Бsanaparva 125. 38-40 and some of the pur─Бnas such as V─Бyu (76.32-34 ) and Brahma (220.150тАУ152) provide that certain consequences follow from the disposal of pindas in one way or another viz. the best worlds by giving pindas to cows, intellect and fame from casting into water, long life from offering them to birds &c. Vide also Brahm─Бnda (upodgh─Бta, chap. 12. 31-35) which provides that if given to cows the result is best complexion, if to cocks then delicacy. long life if given crows. In this connection it should be noted that pindas of rice or of flour were not to be offered in all ┼Ыr─Бddhas. The ┼Ъr─Бddha-kalpalat─Б (pp. 86-89 ) has a long discussion about the ┼Ыr─Бddhas in which the offering of pindas of food is forbidden. For example, it quotes Pulastya to the effect that in ┼Ыr─Бddhas performed on the two ayana days, on the two equinoctial days, on any sankr─Бnti, no pindas are to be offered, so also in ┼Ыr─Бddhas on Ek─Бdasi, Trayodasi, on Magh─Б and Krttik─Б nak┼Яatras, if a man desires to have sons and wealth.

On the question as to what is the principal item in the ┼Ыr─Бddha there are three views. Some, like Govindaraja, 1081 hold that feeding of br─Бhmaс╣Зas is the principal thing and they rely on Manu III. 129 which says ‘One may feed even a single learned br─Бhmaс╣Зa in a rite for gods and manes and not many who do not know vedic mantras; by doing so he reaps abundant reward’. Here the reward or fruit is associated with feeding a learned br─Бhmaс╣Зa. There is a maxim 1082 of the P├╝rvamim─Бс╣Бs─Б that whatever is mentioned in proximity with an action that has a reward or fruit but has no special reward of its own, is subsidiary (anga) to what is declared to have a reward.’ Besides, there is no pindad─Бna in certain ┼Ыr─Бddhas such as ─Бmasr─Бddha, ┼Ыr─Бddha on the Yug─Бdi days.1083

Others like Karka hold the view that pindad─Бna is the principal item in ┼Ыr─Бddha. They rely upon the fact that in the ┼Ыr─Бddha at Gay─Б it is the offering of pindas that is the most important matter and upon the fact that in the Visnudharmas┼лtra (78. 52-53, and 85. 65-66) and in several Pur─Бnas such as the Var─Бha (13.50), Visnu (III. 14.22-23), Brahma (220.31-32), Visnu dharmottara (I. 145.3-4) the pitrs are stated to have expressed a deep yearning for a son who would offer them pindas at Gay─Б and water on sacred rivers &c. (vide note 911). Further support is sought for this view in the fact that in the ┼Ыr─Бddha on the birth of a son and in ┼Ыr─Бddha offered even by a good ┼Ъ┼лdra the feeding of br─Бhmanas is forbidden, A third view is that both the feeding of br├дhmanas and the offering of pindas are the principal matters in a ┼Ыr├дddha. The Gobhila-smrti, after stating 1084 the other two views and some of the reasons therefor, tells us that the author of it is himself in favour of this third view. In cases where the word ┼Ыr─Бddha is employed and there is neither br─Бhmana feeding nor pindad─Бna as in Daiva sr─Бddha, the word ┼Ыr─Бddha is applied in a secondary sense (gauna). Vide Hem─Бdri (┼Ыraddha) pp. 157-160. In the Dharmapradipa it is said that among the followers of the Yajurveda (i. e. V─Бjasaneyins) the offering of pindas is principal, among the followers of the Rgveda the feeding of br─Бhmaс╣Зas is principal, while among the followers of the S─Бmaveda both are principal. In this way ┼Ыr─Бddha partakes of two characters viz. it is a y─Бga (sacrifice) and also 1085 a gift (d─Бna). Haradatta, Hem─Бdri, Kapardi and others appear to hold that all three (bhojana pindad─Бna and agnaukara├▒a) are principal. Vide Samsk├дra ratnam─Бl─Б p. 1003.

Manu (III. 265 ) states 1090 that after the br─Бhmanan have been dismissed the performer of ┼Ыr─Бddha shall offer the (daily) domestic bali offering and that this is the settled rule of dharma. Medh─Бtithi explains that the word ‘bali’ is merely illustrative. The Matsyapur─Б┼Жa 1091 17.61, the Var─Бha pur─Бna (14.43), Skanda VII. 1. 266. 101-102, Devala, K─Бrsn─Бjini and others provide that after the rites for the fathers are finished Vaisvadeva should be performed. When Vai┼бvadeva is performed after the completion of ┼Ыr─Бddha rites, it is to be offered from the food that remains after being utilized for the ┼Ыr─Бddha dinner. But Hem─Бdri (pp. 1058-1065) holds a long discussion and arrives at the following conclusions. In the case of an ─Бhit─Бgni (p. 1064), Vai┼бvadeva is to be performed before ┼Ыr─Бddha except in the case of the ┼Ыr─Бddha on the 11th day after death. In the case of one who has not kept the sacred fires there are three optional times for Vai┼бvadeva, viz. after agnau karaс╣Зa or after the vikira (scattering of food on darbhas for those dying without the sa┼Щsk─Бras being performed for them), or after the br─Бhmanas are dismissed on the completion of the ┼Ыr─Бddha (p. 1064). If Vai┼бvadeva is to be performed before ┼Ыr─Бddha or in the midst of it, then the cooking of food must be done separately for Vai┼бvadeva and for ┼Ыr─Бddha. In the case of all, whether s─Бgnika or anagnika, Vai┼бvadeva must be performed with the remainder of the food left after use in ┼Ыr─Бddha, if the former is performed after the latter. IV)

Modern P─Бrvana┼Ыr─Бddha

485

for the former. The Nirpayasindhu (III. p. 459 ) states that as most smrtis place the performance of Vai┼бvadeva after ┼Ыr─Бddha and as many writers of commentaries and digests such as Medh─Бtithi and Smс╗Щtiratn─Бvali do the same all should perform Vai┼бvadeva after finishing ┼Ыr├дddha.

It is now necessary to illustrate how p─Бrvana sr─Бddha is performed in modern times. Here the greatest variety prevails. The details of the rite vary in the different parts of India. They vary also according as the performer belongs to a particular Veda or a particular recension of the Veda, they vary according to the particular eminent writer that is followed and further additions are made according as the performer is a Vaispava or a Saiva. Such differences have to be passed over here, particularly because they are not material. We saw above that the P─Бrvana-┼Ыr─Бddha was very simple in the days of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas and most of the s┼лtras. There was then no express mention of the worship of Vi┼Ыvedev─Бс╕е in P─Бrvana ┼Ыr─Бddha, or of the maternal ancestors or of the wives of any ancestors. Gradually these came to be added and by the time of the Y─Бj├▒avalkyasmrti there was special invocation of the Vi┼Ыvedev─Бс╕е. But these latter were probably not expressly divided into groups at the time of that work. During the smrti period groups of Vi┼Ыvedev─Бс╕е came to be assigned to different kinds of ┼Ыr├дddhas (vide p. 457 note 1018). The Pur├дpas pres cribed several Paur─Бnic mantras for being recited during the ┼Ыr─Бddha rite, such as the verse S─Бgacchantu’ (note 984) and the verse ‘devat─Бbhyah pitrbhyasca’ (p. 458 note 1020). Then there arose the principle of the P┼лrvami┼Ж─Бms─Б that all rites described in the different s─Бkh─Бs and s┼лtras constitute but one rite, and that one may take over from another s─Бkh─Б or s┼лtra details described therein, which are not opposed to one’s own s─Бkh─Б or sutra (vide pp. 453-55 notes 1011-1013). This principle tended to make the ┼Ыr├дddha rites all inclusive and the whole procedure became swollen to an enormous extent. How even the slightest variation causes difference in the details may be illustrated by an example. In Mithil─Б villages even among poor men eleven br─Бhmaс╣Зas are invited for p─Бrvapa-┼Ыr─Бddha, but it is often difficult to secure a very learned man (who is called p─Бtra or mah─Бp─Бtra) to officiate. In such a case where a mahapatra or a p─Бtra br─Бhmana is not available the ┼Ыr─Бddha be called ap─Бtraka-p─Бrvana┼Ыr├дddha (for which really there is nou┼Ыastric authority) and is distinguished from the sap─Бtraka p─Бrvana ┼Ыr─Бddha in several matters, two of which in the case of the

V─Бjasaneyins may be stated here. In Rudradhara’s Sr─Бddhaviveka (pp. 138-146) the ap─Бtraka p─Бrvana-┼Ыr├дddha-prayoga’ is set out at length.

In medieval and modern times in the different provinces of India different manuals are followed by the followers of the several Vedas. For example, in Bengal the S─Бmavedins, Yajurvedins and Rgvedins follow the procedure of p─Бrvana ┼Ыr─Бddha laid down in the manuals (or paddhatis) of Bhavadeva, Pasupati and K─Бlesi respectively and there are many persons who follow the rules laid down by Raghunandana in his ┼Ъr─Бddhatattva and Yajurvedi┼Ыr─Бddha-tattva In Mithil─Б, ┼Ъr─лdatta wrote his Pit┼Щbhakti for Yajurvedins and the Sr─Бddha kalpa for S─Бmavedins and the Sr─Бddha-ratna of Mah─Бmaho p─Бdhy─Бya Laksm─лpati (between 1500 to 1640 A. D.) which is printed at Darbhanga and claims to be the traditional manual for Maithilas (Maithila-s├дmprad─Бyika-┼Ыr─Бddhapaddhati) in several places says that it follows the Sugatisop─Бna of Prati hastaka for Chandogas and also for V─Бjasaneyins. In the Madras State Vaisnava br─Бhmaс╣Зas follow special treatises on P┼лrva and Apara kriy─Бs of Vaidika-S─Бrvabhauma or Harita Venkat─Бc─Бrya or Tolappar and Smarta br├дhma┼Жas follow the Smrtimukt─Бphala of Vaidyan─Бtha, which does not much differ in major matters from the works of Vaidikas─Бrvabhauma, Often the only differences are in the sankalpa and at the end. It is impossible to exhibit in this work the contents of all these manuals and to compare and contrast them. Therefore I shall set out here a model p─Бrvana┼Ыr─Бddha rite as performed by Revedios in Western India and then a Sukla Yajurveda rite, The Pratis─Бmvatsarika ┼Ыr─Бddha 93 rite for Rgvedins in

The br─Бhmaс╣Зas respond ‘astu vidhivat’ and the per former recites the verse ‘I do obeisance to Acyuta by remem bering whom or by uttering whose name whatever is wanting in tapas (observances) or sacrifices becomes at once perfect’.

Then he says to the pitrya br─Бhmaс╣Зas with your permis sion I shall offer worship to the pitrs’. They reply ‘do offer.’ Then apasavyam. After bending his right knee, the performer says ‘Bh┼лr bhuvah svah to Brahman, this is the seat for my father, grandfather and great-grandfather, named N, N., whose gotra is so and so and who are identical with Vasu, Rudra and Aditya’. So saying he offers double-folded darbhas with sesamum grains to the pitrya br─Бhmaс╣Зas who reply ‘sv─Бsanam’. Then follows the same procedure as regards pitrya br─Бhmanas which has been already set out as to daiva br─Бhmaс╣Зas. The only difference is that instead of two darbhas three darbhas are spread on the ground with their tips towards the south, three vessels are placed towards south-east with faces down wards and three double-folded darbhas are placed on each of the three vessels, instead of ‘yavosi’ the mantra is tilosi somadevatyaс╕е’ (vide note 966) and instead of ‘sv─Бh─Б namah the words “svadh─Б namaс╕е’ are employed, and instead of tulasi leaf bhrngar─Бja leaf is employed. In ─Бv─Бhana the per former places his left hand holding kusas and sesame on the left knee of the pitrya br─Бhmana and the verse repeated is ‘usantas tv─Б’ (Rg. X. 16. 12) as to each pitrya br─Бhmaс╣Зa and he should honour the pitrs by repeating one mantra ‘─Б yantu nah’ (V─Бj. S. 19. 58). He offers arghya 1103 water with the right hand supported by the left to the father and the other two paternal ancestors. Ho brings together the samsravas 1104 in the first pitrya vessel and anoints his face with that water if he desires a son. The br─Бhmaс╣Зas respond ‘may you have a son’.

practised in Madras in these days only a few points of diffe rences in detail emerge. In the Madras procedure the numer ous mantras as set out above (p. 448) do not occur nor does the Tai. ─А, passage occur therein, but the verses in praise of the dust of br─Бhmana’s feet do occur. Most of the mantras both Vedic and Pauranic are the same. The blessings (asir v─Бdas) in the Madras manual are more elaborate and include even the performer’s cattle in the blessing of health and long life. In the Madras manual several mantras are set out as ‘annas─Бkta’ mantras in the procedure itself. The Madras paddhati adds at the end the well known verse ‘k─Бyena v─Бc─Б

manasendriyairva’.

The procedure for Yajurvedins of the M─Бdhyandina Sakha in Bengal as set out by Raghunandana in his Yajurvedi-┼Ыr─Б ddhatattva is entirely based on the 2nd and 3rd kandik─Бs of the Sr─Бddha-s┼лtra of Katy─Бyana. The P─Бryana┼Ыr─Бddha-prayoga in Hal─Бyudha’s Br─Бhmanasarvasva closely follows K─Бty─Бyana and I am assured by a careful student of Dharma┼Ы─Бstra that the pro cedure of p─Бrvana┼Ыr─Бddha followed by Madhyandinas at Bhat para in Western Bengal is in strict conformity with the proce dure laid down by Raghunandana. The Sr─Бddhas┼лtra of K─Бty─Бyana
