“The p─Бrva┼Жa-┼Ыr─Бddha is preceded by the rite for Vi┼бve devas. The procedure follows that of Pindapitryaj├▒a 1124a. In the rites for the pitrs double-folded darbhas are to be used (while in Vai┼бvadevika rite straight darbhas are used). Whenever any thing is to be gifted, the performer (in all daiva as well as pitrya rites ) wears a pavitra and makes the gift sitting. (When questions are to be asked the performer puts the question to the most eminent in the row of diners (to the best daiva br─Бhmana in daiva rites and to the best pitrya br─Бhmaс╣Зa in pitrya rites) or he may put the question to all (and the reply is given by one or by all). Spreading darbhas on the seats (he makes the brahmanas occupy them), he puts the question ‘shal] I invoke the Visvedevas (to the daiva br─Бhmana)’. Being permitted (by the daiva brahmanas) in the words ‘do invoke’, he invokes the Visvedevas with the mantra 1125 Visve dev─Бsa ─Бgata’ (V─Бj. S. 7. 34 ‘Ye All Gods, come, listen to this my call and sit down on this darbha grass ‘). Then he scatters yavas (in front of the br─Бhmaс╣Зas), mutters a mantra Vi┼Ыvedev─Бс╕е srunutemam’ (Vaj. S. 33. 53, ‘Ye All Gods, hear this call of mine’). After this japa he asks (the pitrya br─Бhmaс╣Зas) ‘I shall invoke the pitrs’. When permitted (by the pitrya brah manas) in the words do invoke’, he invokes them with the mantra ‘usantas tva.’ (Vaj. S. 19, 70, ‘O Agni! we longing for our fathers place you down’ &c.). It is to be noted that in the Bengal Manual of P─Бrvana ┼Ыr─Бddha based on the Br─Бhmanasarvasva of Hal─Бyudha and also on Raghunandana’s Yajurvedi-┼Ыr─Бddhatattva the following details are added after the pindas are placed on the darbhas and before the dismissal of the br─Бhmaс╣Зas. He turns towards the north and says ‘O pitrs, regale yourselves here and come like bulls each to his portion.’ Then he turns round to his former position and says ’the pitrs regaled themselves and came like bulls each to his own share.’ Then he loosens 1135 the side of his dhoti which has been tucked up and then folds up his hands (i. e. offers six namask─Бras) with the mantra 1136 ‘Namo vaс╕е pitaro ras─Бya’ (V─Бj. S. I. 32). He smells 1137 the pindas and gives the middle one to his wife, if she desires a son, with the mantra ‘‘─Бdhatta’ (Vaj. S. II. 33).

From considerations of space the procedure of p─Бrva┼Жa ┼Ыr─Бddha among Hiranyake┼Ыins in modern times is passed over here. Moreover, it closely resembles the procedure in ─А┼Ыv. Gr. set out above, the principal difference being that some of the mantras are different. The Samsk├дraratnam─Бl─Б of Gopin─Бtha deals with this from p. 985 onwards. But one noticeable feature of this last work is that of making hair-splitting distinctions. On p. 985 it refers to two ┼Ыr─Бddhas (other than pinda-pitr yaj├▒a) to be performed on am─Бv─Бsy─Б, viz. m─Бsi-┼Ыr┼лddha and m─Бsika-┼Ыr─Бddha, the first being described by the Dharmasutra of Hiranyakesin and the second by the Gshyas┼лtra. laid down by Manu (III. 122) and m─Бsika┼Ыr─Бddha may be per formed after m─Бsi-┼Ыr─Бddha. In modern times no one performs m─Бsi┼Ыr─Бddha or m─Бsika-┼Ыr─Бddha strictly in accordance with the ancient rules. Sr─Бddha is supposed to be performed by feeding a br─Бhmaс╣Зa and giving him a dak┼Яi┼Ж─Б of a few annas. The Sr─Бddhatattva (Jiv., part 1 p. 254) provides, after quoting Matsya and Bhavisya, that, if a person is unable to perform a p─Бrvana┼Ыr─Бddha every month, he should perform one at least thrice a year when the sun is in the zodiacal signs of Kany─Б, Kumbha and Vrsabha and that if he is unable to perform even thrice then he should perform at least once when the sun is in the sign of Kany─Б.

The two meanings of sapi┼Жda given by the Mit, and the D─Бyabh─Бga have already been explained at great length in H. of Dh. vol. II, pp. 452-458 and pp. 472-477. The D─Бyabh─Бga pro pounded the theory that whoever conferred greater spiritual benefit on the deceased by the performance of ┼Ыr─Бddhas and the offering of pindas was entitled to be preferred as an heir to the deceased’s wealth. The Mit. said that heirship depended on blood relationship and the nearest in blood to the deceased was the preferential heir. But even under the Mit. whoever took the wealth of the deceased was bound to pay his debts (Yaj. II, 51 ) and to offer ┼Ыr─Бddha and pinda to him. This subject and the several propositions deduced from the texts have been dealt with in H. of Dh. vol. III, pp. 734-745.

One thing to be remembered is that in determining the preferential right regard is to be had to the capacity of a per son and the efficacy of the pindas when offered. After a person takes the wealth of the deceased, there is no legal machinery to enforce his duty to offer pindas 1138 It was argued in Nalinaksha v. Rajani Kanto 35 C. W. N. 726 that, if an heir does not offer pindas or refuses to offer them to his ancestor. he was not entitled under Hindu Law to succeed to him. This argument was repelled by the judges with the remark that there was no authority for such a proposition and that the right to inheritance is based under the D─Бyabh─Бga not on offering pinda but on the capacity to offer it (p. 729). Vide Gooroo Gobinda Saha v. Anand Lal 5 Beng. L. R. 15 (F. B.) and Digambers Motilal 9 Cal. 563 (F. B.) for the statement that the principle of spiritual benefit is the sole foundation of the theory of in.nl

The Dayabh─Бga theory of spirituat benefit

The question about how ┼Ыr─Бddha was to be performed if one or more of the three paternal ancestors were alive engaged the thoughts of writers from very ancient times. The ─А┼Ыv. 1139 ┼Ъr. S. (II. 6. 16-23) first sets out the views of G─Б┼Жag─Бri, Taulvali and Gautama and then refutes them. G─Б pag─Бri held that out of the three paternal ancestors pindas should be offered to those that were dead and those that were alive should be honoured in person, since the ┼Ыr├дddha rite is meant for pleasing the ancestors; Tau)vali opined that pindas should be offered to all the three ancestors, whether living or dead, since in the rite of ┼Ыr─Бddha they are only a secondary matter (a detail). Gautama thought that pindas should be offered to dead ancestors, upto three from the father if the latter was living, from the grand father if he was alive and from the great-grandfather if all the three be living. ─А┼Ыv. replies; one cannot offer pindas to three ancestors 1110 beyond the father, grand-father or great grandfather, since one has no adhik├дra to do so; one cannot offer pindas to an ancestor after whom there is an ancestor (within three degrees) living. One may offer homa into fire to those that are alive. (If all three ancestors are alive ) all the three pindas must be cast into fire or he may not begin the rite at all. About P─Бrvana┼Ыr─Бddha by jivat pitrka

that one view is that a man whose father is alive cannot engage in a p─Бrvana┼Ыr─Бddha and that the real conclusion is that ┼Ыr─Бddha may be offered to those to whom the father of the performer ) who is living offers pindas. It is clear that one whose father is living should have nothing to do with pindad─Бna for deceased ancestors. Manu (in latter half of III. 220) allowed an alternative viz. one should feed one’s father at a dinner (and honour him with the details of worship such as gandha, dh┼лpa, dipa) and offer pindas to the deceased grandfather and great-grandfather. When any one or two out of the three paternal ancestors are alive and ┼Ыr─Бddha is permitted to a descendant several alternatives become possible by permu tation and combination, which are passed over here from considerations of space and utility. But the various views held by different writers as described above show clearly what a firm grip the theory of the supreme benefits to be derived from ┼Ыr─Бddhas had on the minds not only of common people but of learned men, who, in spite of the fact that the father was alive and was there to offer pindas to his three ancestors, allowed even the son (whose father was living) to offer pindas to the same three ancestors. The Vi┼Я┼Жu Dh. S. extends the procedure about ‘jivatpitrka’ to one’s mother’s paternal ancestors ( changing the mantra where necessary ). 1142a Similar rules apply where the performer’s mother is alive (Agnipur─Бna 117.60’evam m─Бtr─Бdikasy─Бpi tath─Б m─Бt─Бmah─Бdike’).

It is provided by Gobhilasmrti (III. 157) that a ┼Ыruti injunc tion should be made effective by means of anukalpa (of some substituted procedure) if the primary procedure cannot be carried out.1143 If a person cannot secure several br─Бhmaс╣Зas but can secure only one, he should perform P─Бrvana-┼Ыr─Бddha in which six pindas are to be offered with a single br─Бhmaс╣Зa, pro vided he is pankti-p─Бvana 1144 (sanctifier of a row of diners) and in such a case, naivedya should be offered in place of the dinner

IV

Amasr─Бddha and Hema┼Ыr─Бddha

515

svadh─Бk─Бra and dismissal of the brahmanas had to be changed 0. g. in ├дv─Бhana the verse employed is ‘usantastv─Б’ (V─Бj. S. 19.70) which ends with the words тАШhavi┼Яe attave’ (which means

in order to eat the havis’) the words ‘havi┼Яe svikartave’ would have to be substituted.

Amasraddha is to be performed in the first part of the day, ekoddista in the noon, the p─Бrvana┼Ыr─Бddha in the afternoon and yrddhi┼бr─Бddha in the first part of the day (divided into five ). 1149a

If even uncooked food grains cannot be offered the per formier should perform hema┼Ыr─Бddha (┼Ыr├дddha with money ). When the sun passes from one sign of the zodiac into another, in default of food and br─Бhmaс╣Зas, on a journey, on the birth of a son, in an eclipse, in the case of women and s├╝dras hema ┼Ыr─Бddha is allowed or when one’s wife is in her monthly illness. In ─Бma┼Ыr─Бddha twice the quantity of grains required in offering cooked food and in hema┼Ыr─Бddha four times (the price of the grains required for cooked food) has to be offered. If no money can be had the digests prescribe several modes which have already been set out above ( vide p. 425, n. 955).
